State v. Pruitt


No. M2013-02393-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


510 S.W.3d 398; 2016 Tenn. LEXIS 980


May 25, 2016, Session Heard at Cookeville1


1 We heard oral argument in this case on May 25, 2016, at Tennessee Technological University in Cookeville, Tennessee, as part of this Court's S.C.A.L.E.S. (Supreme Court Advancing Legal Education for Students) project.

 
December 30, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 11 [**1] Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals Circuit Court for Hickman County. No. 11-5005-CR. Timothy L. Easter, Judge.
State v. Pruitt, 2015 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 688 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 26, 2015)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether application of the Tennessee Exclusionary Rule Reform Act (ERRA), Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-6-108, to validate the search warrant in defendant's case was an ex post facto violation under U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, cl. 1, and Tenn. Const. art. I, § 11. HOLDINGS: [1]-The ERRA was not an ex post facto statute as applied in defendant's case. As a result, defendant's motion to suppress the evidence against him, under Tenn. R. Crim. P. 41, was not well-taken because the error in the date written on the search warrant in the case was a good faith or technical mistake and the trial court properly ruled that, pursuant to the ERRA, the evidence was not to be suppressed; [2]-The evidence supported defendant's convictions for first degree premeditated murder, attempted first degree premeditated murder, and aggravated assault and the jury's rejection of defendant's self-defense claim.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the intermediate appellate court affirmed.

 

2 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Davidson


No. E2013-00394-SC-DDT-DD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


509 S.W.3d 156; 2016 Tenn. LEXIS 913


January 27, 2016, Session 
December 19, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Davidson v. Tenn., 2017 U.S. LEXIS 5551 (U.S., Oct. 2, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(a)(1) Automatic Appeal; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed in Part and Vacated in Part. Automatic Appeal from the Court of Criminal Appeals. Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 86216B. Walter C. Kurtz, Senior Judge. [**1] 1


1 Judge Richard Baumgartner was the trial judge in this case until he resigned in March 2011. This Court appointed Senior Judge Jon Kerry Blackwood and subsequently Senior Judge Walter C. Kurtz to preside over the case.


State v. Davidson, 2015 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 164 (Tenn. Crim. App., Mar. 10, 2015)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed in Part and Vacated in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress evidence obtained from the search of his house, as the officer intended to obtain a valid search warrant, reasonably believed that the warrant, based on probable cause and issued by a neutral and detached magistrate, was valid, and stopped the search and obtained a second warrant supported by a properly signed affidavit, as required by Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 40-6-103, 40-6-104 and Tenn. R. Crim. P. 41(c)(1), once he learned of the problem; [2]-The trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress statements, as defendant was read his Miranda rights, voluntarily waived them, and was not coerced given that he had above average intelligence, the interview was not unreasonably lengthy, he was not impaired, and officers statements regarding cooperation were made after defendant waived his rights.


OUTCOME: Affirmed in part, vacated in part.

 

3 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Martinez v. Lawhon


No. M2015-00635-SC-R3-WC


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, SPECIAL WORKERS' COMPENSATION APPEALS PANEL, AT NASHVILLE


2016 Tenn. LEXIS 840


March 21, 2016, Session 
November 21, 2016, Filed


NOTICE: CONSULT THE TENNESSEE SUPREME COURT RULES FOR CITATION OF UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by, Adopted by Martinez v. Lawhon, 2016 Tenn. LEXIS 839 (Tenn., Nov. 21, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-225(a)(2) [*1] (2014) Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 131145IV. Russell T. Perkins, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The permanent partial disability benefits for an employee who could to return to work due to federal immigration law were limited by Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-241(e)(2) to a cap of one and one-half times the medical impairment rating; [2]-Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-241(e) applied to the instant case where the establishment of an evidentiary presumption as to whether an employer's original hiring was knowing did not affect the legal standard for the maximum compensation due to an injured undocumented worker; [3]-Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-241(e)(2)(B)(ii) was preempted by 8 U.S.C.S. § 1324a(h)(2) as it imposed a civil penalty on an employer; [4]-Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-241(e)(2)(B)(ii) could not be severed; [5]-Under Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-241(d), the employee was not capped, and the evidence supported the impairment rating and permanent partial disability award.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

4 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Whited


No. E2013-02523-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


506 S.W.3d 416; 2016 Tenn. LEXIS 823


January 27, 2016, Session 
November 7, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 11 [**1] Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Criminal Court and the Court of Criminal Appeals Reversed; Case Remanded to the Criminal Court. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 100430. Steven Wayne Sword, Judge.
State v. Whited, 2015 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 324 (Tenn. Crim. App., May 4, 2015)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court and the Court of Criminal Appeals Reversed; Case Remanded to the Criminal Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant's convictions for especially aggravated sexual exploitation of a minor under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-1005, had to be reversed because the videos defendant secretly took of his daughter and her friend using a cell phone he placed in the daughter's bedroom and bathroom, while depicting the daughter and the friend in the nude, did not include a minor engaging in a lascivious exhibition but rather in everyday activities such as showering and changing clothes; [2]-Double jeopardy did not preclude retrial on charges of attempted especially production of child pornography, as the evidence was sufficient to support a conviction for the lesser offense.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded.

 

5 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Reynolds


No. E2013-02309-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


504 S.W.3d 283; 2016 Tenn. LEXIS 821


September 30, 2015, Session1


1 Oral arguments were held on the campus of Cumberland University in Lebanon, Tennessee, as part of this Court's S.C.A.L.E.S. (Supreme Court Advancing Legal Education for Students) project.

 
November 3, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 11 [**1] Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 99372. Steven Wayne Sword, Judge.
State v. Reynolds, 2014 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1024 (Tenn. Crim. App., Nov. 12, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the warrantless blood draw from defendant, following an automobile accident in which defendant was driving, violated defendant's right to be free from unreasonable searches and seizures, guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. IV and Tenn. Const. art. I, § 7. HOLDINGS: [1]-The sheriff's deputy had probable cause to believe that defendant was driving while intoxicated at the time of the accident. Thus the implied consent statute was triggered; [2]-Even if the warrantless blood draw violated defendant's federal and state constitutional right to be free from unreasonable searches and seizures, the good-faith exception to the exclusionary rule was adopted, and as a result, any evidence derived from testing defendant's blood need not have been suppressed because the warrantless blood draw was obtained in objectively reasonable good-faith reliance on binding precedent.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the intermediate appellate court affirmed, and case remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

State v. Willis


No. E2012-01313-SC-DDT-DD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


496 S.W.3d 653; 2016 Tenn. LEXIS 405


October 1, 2015, Session Heard at Nashville 
July 6, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ dismissed by Willis v. State, 2016 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 488 (Tenn. Crim. App., July 7, 2016)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Willis v. Tenn., 2017 U.S. LEXIS 1710 (U.S., Mar. 6, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(a)(1) [**1] (2014); Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Automatic Appeal from the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Washington County. No. 28343. Jon Kerry Blackwood, Judge.
State v. Willis, 2015 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 169 (Tenn. Crim. App., Mar. 13, 2015)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-There was no Sixth Amendment violation with respect to incriminating statements defendant made to his ex-wife where he failed to prove an explicit or implicit arrangement between the ex-wife and law enforcement officers for her to act as an agent of the government in her January 1, 2003 meeting with defendant in New York, as the evidence showed that officers advised her not to accede to defendant's request that she visit him in New York but she went anyway and she did not record the conversation; [2]-Admission of incriminating statements defendant made to ex-wife did not violate his Sixth Amendment rights where, by placing the telephone calls to his ex-wife with full knowledge that they were subject to monitoring and recording by the jail, defendant voluntarily, knowingly, and intelligently waived his rights.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Smith


No. M2013-02818-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE1


1 We heard oral argument in this case on September 30, 2015, at Cumberland University in Lebanon, Tennessee, as part of the S.C.A.L.E.S. (Supreme Court Advancing Legal Education for Students) project.


484 S.W.3d 393; 2016 Tenn. LEXIS 92


September 30, 2015, Session 
February 11, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 11 [**1] ; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Appeal from the Court of Criminal Appeals. Circuit Court for Williamson County. No. II-CR077410. James G. Martin, III, Judge.
State v. Smith, 2015 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 70 (Tenn. Crim. App., Feb. 2, 2015)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The totality of the circumstances surrounding the traffic stop, including the fact that it was 3:00 a.m., defendant was driving on dry roads, and defendant was driving on a highway with clearly marked lanes, established a reasonable suspicion, supported by specific and articulable facts that defendant violated Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-8-123(1) when she crossed the fog line and failed to remain entirely within her lane of travel, and thus, the officer's stop was justified and defendant's motion to suppress properly denied.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

9 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Mortgage Elec. Registration Sys. v. Ditto


No. E2012-02292-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


488 S.W.3d 265; 2015 Tenn. LEXIS 1000


May 5, 2015, Session 
December 11, 2015, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 11 [**1] Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals, Eastern Section, Chancery Court for Hamilton County. No. 120058. W. Frank Brown III, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A trial court did not err in denying a borrower's motion to dismiss an action seeking to avoid a tax sale for lack of notice because when a plaintiff who claimed to have a protected interest in real property filed suit to set aside a tax sale for lack of notice, the pre-suit tender requirement in Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-5-2504(c) (2011) did not apply; [2]-MERS acquired no protected interest in the subject property by virtue of language in the deed of trust (DOT) designating it as beneficiary solely as nominee for the lender and its assigns, or by language in the DOT indicating that MERS had legal title of the subject property for the purpose of enforcing the lender's rights; [3]-Because MERS had no protected interest in the subject property, its due process rights were not violated by the county's failure to notify it of the tax foreclosure proceedings or the tax sale.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

10 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brown


No. E2014-00673-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


479 S.W.3d 200; 2015 Tenn. LEXIS 933


September 10, 2015, Session 
December 2, 2015, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 11 [**1] Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for McMinn County. Nos. 95857, 95858, 95859, 95860. Carroll L. Ross, Judge.
State v. Brown, 2014 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 983 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 29, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Appellant former inmate was not entitled to relief from an expired illegal sentence because Tenn. R. Crim. P. 36.1 did not expand the relief available for illegal sentence claims to include correcting expired illegal sentences, as such relief was traditionally available by way of habeas corpus, requiring a petitioner to be in custody, under Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-21-101(a) (2012), and the former inmate's motion alleging a failure to award pretrial jail credit under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-23-101(c) stated no colorable claim for relief from an illegal sentence, under Tenn. R. Crim. P. 36.1, as this did not render the sentence illegal; [2]-The former inmate was entitled to have a clerical error corrected to reflect the imposition of a shorter sentence because the trial court violated Tenn. R. Crim. P. 11(c) by imposing a sentence exceeding that agreed to in his plea bargain.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

11 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Chattanooga-Hamilton Cnty. Hosp. Auth. v. UnitedHealthcare Plan of the River Valley, Inc.


No. M2013-00942-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


475 S.W.3d 746; 2015 Tenn. LEXIS 913


February 4, 2015, Session 
November 5, 2015, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 11 [**1] Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Reversed, Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part, and Case Remanded For Further Proceedings. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals, Middle Section, Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 091253II. Carol L. McCoy, Chancellor.
Chattanooga-Hamilton County Hosp. Auth. v. United Healthcare Plan of the River Valley, Inc., 2014 Tenn. App. LEXIS 332 (Tenn. Ct. App., June 6, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Reversed, Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part, and Case Remanded For Further Proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The appellate court erred in dismissing a hospital's claim for monies due under Tenn. Code Ann. § 71-5-108 (2012) for emergency services provided to the enrollees of a managed care organization (MCO) because the parties' claims would necessarily require the trial court to render a declaratory judgment concerning the validity or applicability of the 74% and 57% rules in Tenn. Comp. R. & Regs. 1200-13-13-.08(2)(b) and (c), a request for declaratory judgment regarding the applicability or validity of the regulations was implicit in the hospital's claims for money damages, and the MCO's counterclaim appeared to present the other side of the same coin, and the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction to hear the case under Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-5-225 (2015) where the hospital failed to exhaust its administrative remedies.


OUTCOME: Appellate judgment reversed, trial judgment affirmed in part and reversed in part, and case remanded.

 

12 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Turner v. Turner


No. W2013-01833-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


473 S.W.3d 257; 2015 Tenn. LEXIS 831


June 2, 2015, Session Heard at Nashville 
October 21, 2015, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 11 [**1] Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part; Case Remanded. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals, Western Section Chancery Court for Fayette County. No. 12354. Martha Brasfield, Chancellor.
Turner v. Turner, 2014 Tenn. App. LEXIS 398 (Tenn. Ct. App., July 7, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Tennessee statutes authorize dispensing with personal service of process in a proceeding to terminate parental rights only if the defendant's residence is unknown and cannot be ascertained upon diligent inquiry, Tenn. Code Ann. § 21-1-203(a)(5) (2009), and the plaintiff has asked for an order authorizing constructive service by publication and has supported the request with an affidavit, Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-117(m)(3) (2014); [2]-The record contained neither a motion from the father requesting an order authorizing constructive service by publication nor an affidavit describing the diligent inquiries that were made; [3]-The father's failure to comply with the statutory requirements necessary for resorting to constructive service by publication deprived the trial court of personal jurisdiction over the mother, and the judgment terminating the mother's rights was void.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part, case remanded.

 

13 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Clark v. Cain


No. E2015-00949-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


479 S.W.3d 830; 2015 Tenn. LEXIS 829



October 16, 2015, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Circuit Court for Hamilton County. No. 12C1147CV.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court erred in considering the defendants' motion for partial summary judgment and the plaintiffs' constitutional challenge to Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-39-102 because the matter was premature where the statutory cap on non-economic damages would have no relevance in the case unless and until the plaintiffs obtained a verdict in excess of that cap, whether the cap was implicated in the case thus remained an open question, and the issue of the constitutionality of that cap was not ripe for determination, and such consideration properly should await a verdict in favor of the plaintiffs in excess of the statutory cap, should the same occur.


OUTCOME: Applications granted, judgment vacated, and case remanded.

 

14 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Ellithorpe v. Weismark


No. M2014-00279-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


479 S.W.3d 818; 2015 Tenn. LEXIS 827


June 3, 2015, Session 
October 8, 2015, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 11 [**1] Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Reversed; Judgment of the Trial Court Reinstated. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals, Middle Section, Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 13C2775. Thomas W. Brothers, Judge.
Ellithorpe v. Weismark, 2014 Tenn. App. LEXIS 709 (Tenn. Ct. App., Oct. 31, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Reversed; Judgment of the Trial Court Reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Tennessee Civil Justice Act of 2011, which amended the Tennessee Health Care Liability Act (THCLA), Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-26-101 et seq., statutorily abrogated the decision in Estate of French v. Stratford House, 333 S.W.3d 546 (Tenn. 2011) and the nuanced approach for distinguishing ordinary negligence and health care liability claims as outlined in that case, by providing that any such civil action is subject to the THCLA regardless of any other claims or theories alleged in the complaint; [2]- Plaintiffs' allegations against a social worker met the definition of a health care liability action under Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-26-101(a)(1) and expert testimony would be required; [3]-Because plaintiffs failed to provide pre-suit notice or file a certificate of good faith, for purposes of Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 29-26-121, 29-26-122, dismissal with prejudice was warranted.


OUTCOME: Appellate court judgment reversed, trial court judgment reinstated.

State v. Bell


No. W2012-02017-SC-DDT-DD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


512 S.W.3d 167; 2015 Tenn. LEXIS 720


March 4, 2015, Session 
September 10, 2015, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Bell v. Tennessee, 136 S. Ct. 2006, 195 L. Ed. 2d 221, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 3192 (U.S., May 16, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Automatic Appeal from the Court of Criminal Appeals Circuit Court for Tipton County. No. 6664 Joe H. Walker, Judge. Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(a)(1) [**1] ; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.
State v. Bell, 2014 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 508 (Tenn. Crim. App., May 30, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether defendant was properly convicted and sentenced to death for first degree felony murder. HOLDINGS: [1]-The defense failed to carry its burden of proving that defendant suffered from an intellectual disability that rendered him ineligible for the death penalty under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-203(b) (2010); [2]-Tennessee's intellectual disability statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-203, as then interpreted, was constitutionally sound under U.S. Const. amend. VIII; [3]-While the trial court erred when it refused to allow the defense to cross-examine the victim's husband about his affair with his former wife, the err was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt; [4]-The evidence was sufficient to support the jury's conclusion that the victim was killed after being forced to leave her residence; [10]-The death sentence imposed in the case was not excessive or disproportionate.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

16 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Teats


No. M2012-01232-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


468 S.W.3d 495; 2015 Tenn. LEXIS 559


February 5, 2015, Session 
July 14, 2015, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 11 [**1] Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2009D2955. Steve R. Dozier, Judge.
State v. Teats, 2014 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 18 (Tenn. Crim. App., Jan. 10, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court did not err in declining to give the jury instruction that was used when the jury had to determine whether the removal or confinement was, in essence, incidental to the accompanying felony or, in the alternative, was significant enough, standing alone, to support a conviction because the instruction was not required when a defendant was charged with the offenses of kidnapping and robbery of different victims; [2]-Because the State charged defendant with robbing a restaurant manager and kidnapping four other employees, defendant did not stand the risk of being convicted of kidnapping a victim he confined only long enough to rob; [3]-The due process concerns were not present because the kidnapping of one or more victims could never be essentially incidental to an offense perpetrated against a different victim or victims.


OUTCOME: Convictions affirmed.

 

17 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


West v. Schofield


No. M2014-02478-SC-R10-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


468 S.W.3d 482; 2015 Tenn. LEXIS 548


May 6, 2015, Session Heard at Knoxville 
July 2, 2015, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 10 [**1] Extraordinary Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed; Electrocution Causes of Action Dismissed. Appeal by Permission from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 131627I. Claudia Bonnyman, Chancellor.
West v. Schofield, 2015 Tenn. LEXIS 172 (Tenn., Feb. 13, 2015)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Reversed; Electrocution Causes of Action Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendants were death-sentenced inmates who challenged the constitutionality of electrocution as a method of execution in Tennessee; [2]-The electrocution causes of action were dismissed, as nothing demonstrated that defendants were presently subject to execution by electrocution; [3]-The plain language of the Capital Punishment Enforcement Act established that none of defendants would ever become subject to execution by electrocution unless one of two statutory contingencies actually occurred, as set forth in Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-23-114(e), and defendants did not show that either contingency had occurred; [4]-The electrocution causes of action were not ripe for judicial decision because they involved a method of execution that did not presently apply to defendants and would never apply to them unless one of the two statutory contingencies occurred in the future.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed, electrocution causes of action dismissed.

 

18 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Burgins


No. E2014-02110-SC-R8-CO


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


464 S.W.3d 298; 2015 Tenn. LEXIS 285


February 5, 2015, Session 
April 7, 2015, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 8 [**1] Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Reversed; Case Remanded to the Trial Court. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals, Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 101255. Bobby R. McGee, Judge.
State v. Burgins, 2014 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1089 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 3, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Reversed; Case Remanded to the Trial Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether defendant forfeited the constitutional right to pretrial bail by engaging in criminal conduct while released on bond. HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant had a constitutional right to pretrial bail, under Tenn. Const. art. I, § 15, but this right was not absolute and was subject to forfeiture. Therefore, remand of the case to the trial court was required for a bail revocation hearing, pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-11-141(b), to be conducted expeditiously according to the procedure established in compliance with the requirements of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Tenn. Const. art. I, § 8.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed, and case remanded for a bail revocation hearing.

 

19 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hall


No. M2012-00336-SC-DDT-DD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


461 S.W.3d 469; 2015 Tenn. LEXIS 241


October 9, 2014, Session 
March 20, 2015, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Hall v. Tenn., 2015 U.S. LEXIS 7117 (U.S., Nov. 9, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(a)(1) [**1] (2014); Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Automatic Appeal from the Court of Criminal Appeals Circuit Court for Humphreys County. Nos. 10526, 10527, 10556, 10557, 10558, 10559. Jon Kerry Blackwood, Sr. Judge.
State v. Hall, 2013 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 920 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 22, 2013)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The original judge denied defendant's original motion for new trial in 1992, nearly 20 years before his death, and thus the only motion for new trial that was filed during the effective date of the prior statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 17-1-305 (1980), was not undisposed of at the time of the original judge's death; [2]-The new and amended motions for new trial would not satisfy the plain language of the 1980 statute because those motions were not presented to the original judge within 30 days of sentences; [3]-Because none of defendant's motions for new trial fell within the scope of the prior statute, its terms were inapplicable; [4]-The successor judge did not abuse his discretion by denying the re-asserted petition for writ of error coram nobis under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-26-105(b) (2012) because defendant was not entitled to a new trial based upon newly discovered evidence.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

20 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


West v. Schofield


No. M2014-00320-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


460 S.W.3d 113; 2015 Tenn. LEXIS 178


December 18, 2014, Session 
March 10, 2015, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by West v. Schofield, 2017 Tenn. LEXIS 185 (Tenn., Mar. 28, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 11 [**1] Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Reversed; Remanded. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals, Middle Section Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 13-1627-I. Claudia C. Bonnyman, Chancellor.
West v. Schofield, 2014 Tenn. App. LEXIS 609 (Tenn. Ct. App., Sept. 29, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Reversed; Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The identities of the John Doe defendants, persons involved in facilitating and carrying out executions of inmates, were not relevant to a determination of the constitutionality of the lethal injection protocol as written, and therefore the lower courts erred by discovery of defendants' identities under Tex. R. Civ. P. 26, because the identities of persons who facilitated or carried out the protocol were not relevant to a determination of whether the protocol passed constitutional muster; [2]-Even if the inmates had sufficiently alleged that the protocol was unconstitutional as applied to one or more of them or that one or more individuals may cause the protocol to be carried out in an unconstitutional manner in the future, the claims were hypothetical and speculative and did not constitute a justiciable controversy under the Declaratory Judgments Act.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and case remanded.

 

21 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Crank


No. E2012-01189-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


468 S.W.3d 15; 2015 Tenn. LEXIS 109


September 4, 2014, Session 
February 13, 2015, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 11 [**1] Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals, Circuit Court for Loudon County. No. 10611B. E. Eugene Eblen, Judge.
State v. Crank, 2013 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 828 (Tenn. Crim. App., Sept. 26, 2013)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The court of appeals properly affirmed defendant's conviction for child neglect under the child abuse and neglect statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-15-401 (2014), based upon her failure to obtain medical treatment for her child because defendant did not qualify for the spiritual treatment exemption, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-15-402(c) (2014); [2]-Because the exemption was effectively limited to members of religious groups that closely resembled the Christian Science Church, its terms were not so vague that the scope of the exemption could not be ascertained; [3]-Because the exemption protected only those individuals who fit within its specific criteria, the statutes did not simultaneously authorize and prohibit the same conduct; [4]-Enforcing the child abuse and neglect statute without the spiritual treatment exemption was consistent with the expressed legislative intent.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

22 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Durham v. Tenn. DOL & Workforce Dev.


No. M2014-00428-SC-R10-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2015 Tenn. LEXIS 20



January 14, 2015, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at, Remanded by Durham v. Tenn. DOL & Workforce Dev., 2015 Tenn. App. LEXIS 97 (Tenn. Ct. App., Feb. 27, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 06C95.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Court of Appeals properly denied an employee's application for recusal of all appellate judges and justices because she provided no supporting documents of any kind, and assuming only for the sake of argument that all of the appellate judges and justices had some personal interest in the outcome of the employee's second appeal that might require their recusal, the "Rule of Necessity" applied, and they could not recuse themselves; [2]-The Court of Appeals properly denied the employee's motion to reconsider the denial of her motion to consolidate her two appeals because the two appeals had nothing in common but for the identity of employee.


OUTCOME: Application and motion denied.

 

23 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. McCoy


No. M2013-00912-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


459 S.W.3d 1; 2014 Tenn. LEXIS 942


February 6, 2014, Session 
December 1, 2014, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission from Denial of Rule 9 [**1] Application; Judgment of the Trial Court Reversed; Case Remanded to the Trial Court. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals. Circuit Court for Montgomery County. No. 41001277 John H. Gasaway, III, Judge.
State v. McCoy, 2013 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1157 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 5, 2013)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court Reversed; Case Remanded to the Trial Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The supreme court held that Tenn. Code Ann. § 24-7-123 does not frustrate or interfere with the adjudicative function of Tennessee courts, as it served as a specific and limited exception to the general rule against the admission of hearsay evidence, and Tenn. R. Evid. 802 recognizes that sources of law outside of the Tennessee Rules of Evidence may develop such an exception; [2]-Although the video-recorded interview of the victim qualified as hearsay, it was admissible under § 24-7-123, as a valid legislative exception to the general rule excluding hearsay; [3]-The admission of the child victim's video-recorded statements would not violate defendant's right to confrontation if the child appeared as a witness, authenticated the video recording, and appeared for cross-examination.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded.

 

24 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dotson


No. W2011-00815-SC-DDT-DD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


450 S.W.3d 1; 2014 Tenn. LEXIS 694


April 9, 2014, Session 
September 30, 2014, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Dotson v. Tennessee, 2015 U.S. LEXIS 1830 (U.S., Mar. 9, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(a)(1) [**1] ; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Automatic appeal from the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 0807688. James C. Beasley, Jr., Judge.
State v. Dotson, 2013 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 584 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 25, 2013)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a death penalty case in which the jury convicted defendant of six counts of premeditated first degree murder for killing his brother, three other adults, and two of his brother's minor sons, under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(c)(1)(C), the aggravating circumstances as to each of the murders outweighed any mitigating circumstances and justified imposition of the death penalty; [2]-Under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(c)(1)(D), the sentences of death were not excessive or disproportionate to the penalties imposed in similar cases as the proof showed that defendant shot and killed his brother and three other adults; defendant then stabbed and beat with wooden boards his four nephews and his niece, who ranged in age from nine years to two months old; the unprovoked attacks on the children were both cruel and brutal; and defendant never attempted to render aid or summon help.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

25 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Freeland


No. W2011-01828-SC-DDT-DD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


451 S.W.3d 791; 2014 Tenn. LEXIS 640


April 10, 2014, Session Heard at McKenzie1


1 Oral argument was heard in this case on April 10, 2014, at Bethel University in McKenzie, Tennessee, as part of this Court's S.C.A.L.E.S. (Supreme Court Advancing Legal Education for Students) project.

 
September 17, 2014, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Freeland v. Tennessee, 2015 U.S. LEXIS 1112 (U.S., Feb. 23, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(a)(1) [**1] ; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed; Case Remanded to the Trial Court for Entry of a Corrected Judgment. Automatic Appeal from the Court of Criminal Appeals Circuit Court for Madison County. No. 10-409. Roy B. Morgan, Jr., Judge.
State v. Freeland, 2013 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 463 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 3, 2013)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed; Case Remanded to the Trial Court for Entry of a Corrected Judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In defendant's death penalty case, he voluntarily waived his Miranda rights under U.S. Const. amend. V because defendant signed the rights waiver form before each of the four interviews began, and the record was devoid of any evidence that defendant was coerced, threatened, or tricked into signing any of the waivers; [2]-Defendant's confession was voluntary under U.S. Const. amend. V because he was twenty-eight years old, he had completed college courses, he was familiar with the legal system, none of the interviews were prolonged, and defendant was not abused, threatened, or deprived of food, sleep, or medical attention; [3]-Defendant's sentence of death was not disproportionate under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204 because defendant's case, taken as a whole, was not plainly lacking in circumstances consistent with other cases in which the death penalty was imposed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the case was remanded to the trial court for entry of a corrected judgment.

State v. Jackson


No. W2009-01709-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


444 S.W.3d 554; 2014 Tenn. LEXIS 619


November 6, 2013, Session 
August 22, 2014, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 11 [**1] Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Reversed in Part; Conviction Vacated; and Case Remanded to the Trial Court. Appeal by permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 05-05757. Chris Craft, Judge.
State v. Jackson, 2012 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1003 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 10, 2012)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Reversed in Part; Conviction Vacated; and Case Remanded to the Trial Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether defendant was properly convicted of second degree murder. HOLDINGS: [1]-The lead prosecutor's remark during final closing argument at trial amounted to a constitutionally impermissible comment upon defendant's exercise of her constitutional right, under Tenn. Const. art. I, § 9 and U.S. Const. amend. V, to remain silent and not testify; [2]-The prosecution violated defendant's constitutional right to due process, under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, by failing to turn over until after trial the third statement a key witness gave to law enforcement officers investigating the murder; [3]-The State of Tennessee failed to establish that the constitutional errors were harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: Conviction and sentence vacated, and case remanded for a new trial.

Long v. Bd. of Prof'l Responsibility of the Supreme Court of Tenn.


No. M2013-01042-SC-R3-BP


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


435 S.W.3d 174; 2014 Tenn. LEXIS 444


February 5, 2014, Session 
June 4, 2014, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal Pursuant to Tenn. Sup. Ct. R. 9, § 1.3; Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Montgomery County. No. MCCHCVMG1216. Don R. Ash, Senior Judge.
Ferrell v. Long, 2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 217 (Tenn. Ct. App., May 14, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The hearing panel's finding that the attorney violated Tenn. Sup. Ct. R. Prof. Conduct 8, 1.15(a), 1.16, 8.4, and 1.4(a) was supported by substantial and material evidence because the attorney and his client gave conflicting testimony on whether the written fee agreement was subsequently modified by an oral agreement that permitted the attorney to treat $ 7,500 as an earned fee and the hearing panel credited the client's version of events; [2]-The court rejected the attorney's contention that Tenn. Sup. Ct. R. 9 was unconstitutional because it did not violate due process, as the investigatory/enforcement responsibilities and the adjudicative responsibilities were functionally separate within the Board of Professional Responsibility; [3]-Tenn. Sup. Ct. R. 9, § 24 did not create a financial incentive for the board to initite formal disciplinary proceedings.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Hooker v. Haslam


No. M2012-01299-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


437 S.W.3d 409; 2014 Tenn. LEXIS 195


July 19, 2013, Session 
March 17, 2014, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Hooker v. Haslam, 2014 Tenn. LEXIS 934 (Tenn., Apr. 23, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Vacated in Part, Affirmed in Part. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals, Middle Section, Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 12C-735. Hamilton V. Gayden, Judge.
Hooker v. Haslam, 382 S.W.3d 358, 2012 Tenn. App. LEXIS 511 (Tenn. Ct. App., 2012)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Vacated in Part, Affirmed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether certain provisions of the Tennessee Plan, Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 17-4-101 through 17-4-119 (2009), which governed the way in which Tennessee appellate judges were initially selected and thereafter stood for reelection, violated the Tennessee Constitution. HOLDINGS: [1]-The issue of the constitutional validity of the Judicial Nominating Commission/gubernatorial appointment process under the Tennessee Plan was moot; [2]-The retention election portion of the Tennessee Plan satisfied the constitutional requirement that the judges of the appellate courts be elected by the qualified voters of the State of Tennessee and did not violate the Tennessee Constitution; [3]-The election of judges to the Tennessee Court of Appeals and the Court of Criminal Appeals of Tennessee on a statewide basis did not violate the Tennessee Constitution.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the intermediate appellate court vacated in part and affirmed in part.

State v. Pollard


No. M2011-00332-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


432 S.W.3d 851; 2013 Tenn. LEXIS 1011


October 2, 2013, Session 
December 20, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed; Case Remanded to the Trial Court. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals. Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2006D2820. Monte Watkins, Judge.
State v. Pollard, 2012 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 749 (Tenn. Crim. App., Sept. 17, 2012)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed; Case Remanded to the Trial Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The court of criminal appeals did not err in remanding the case to the trial court for a proper determination of whether defendant's sentences had to be served consecutively or concurrently because it failed to address the factors required to impose consecutive sentences based on the dangerous offender classification under the Tennessee Criminal Sentencing Reform Act of 1989, Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-115(b)(4); [2]-The trial court failed to demonstrate that the imposition of consecutive sentences reasonably related to the severity of the offenses or that the total sentence was necessary to protect the public from defendant; [3]-When a trial court placed findings on the record to support its sentencing decision the applicable standard of appellate review for a challenge to the imposition of consecutive sentences was abuse of discretion with a presumption of reasonableness.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed and cause remanded.

Cooper v. Glasser


No. M2012-00344-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


419 S.W.3d 924; 2013 Tenn. LEXIS 991


May 31, 2013, Session 
November 26, 2013, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 31, 2014.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Reversed; Case Remanded. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals, Middle Section Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 11C3952. Joseph P. Binkley Jr., Judge.
Cooper v. Glasser, 2012 Tenn. App. LEXIS 723 (Tenn. Ct. App., Oct. 12, 2012)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Reversed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A plaintiff's state law suit, in which he alleged fraud, promissory estoppel, and breach-of-contract claims that he had previously dismissed in both California and federal court, was governed by Tennessee claim-preclusion law because the federal court did not pass on the substantive merits, and permitting him to pursue his suit in Tennessee was not incompatible with federal interests; [2]-Tennessee law did not give claim-preclusive effect to the plaintiff's second voluntary dismissal in federal court, because Tenn. R. Civ. P. 41.01(1) permitted a plaintiff to voluntarily dismiss his case two times without prejudice.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed.

City of Memphis v. Hargett


No. M2012-02141-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


414 S.W.3d 88; 2013 Tenn. LEXIS 779


February 6, 2013, Session 
October 17, 2013, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Substituted opinion at City of Memphis v. Hargett, 2013 Tenn. LEXIS 1101 (Tenn., Oct. 17, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals, Middle Section, Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 121269II. Carol L. McCoy, Chancellor.
City of Memphis v. Hargett, 2012 Tenn. App. LEXIS 742 (Tenn. Ct. App., Oct. 25, 2012)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The 2013 amendments to the Tennessee Voter Identification Act (the Act), Tenn. Code Ann. § 2-7-112(a)(1)(B), rendered moot all issues pertaining to the validity of the photo identification (ID) cards issued by a city library that were being challenged; [2]-The individual voters, but not the city, demonstrated standing to challenge the constitutionality of the Act; [3]-Although the individual voters' constitutional claims qualified as justiciable, the Court found no basis for invalidating the Act on constitutional grounds; [4]-The Court held that the photo ID requirement under the Act was a logical method of protecting the integrity of elections by combating in-person voter fraud and was a narrowly tailored means for the State to guard against the risk of voter impersonation by ensuring that voters are who they say they are.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

City of Memphis v. Hargett

SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2013 Tenn. LEXIS 1101


February 6, 2013, Session 
October 17, 2013, Filed

City of Memphis v. Hargett, 414 S.W.3d 88, 2013 Tenn. LEXIS 779 (Tenn., 2013)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed.

Code Ann. § 2-7-112(a)(1)(B) (Supp. 2012) (amended 2013). OUTCOME: Judgment of the intermediate appellate court affirmed.

State v. Pruitt


No. W2009-01255-SC-DDT-DD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


415 S.W.3d 180; 2013 Tenn. LEXIS 778


April 3, 2013, Session 
October 8, 2013, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for certiorari filed at, 03/17/2014


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(a)(1); Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Automatic Appeal from the Court of Criminal Appeals, Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 06-00460. Chris B. Craft, Judge.
State v. Pruitt, 2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 431 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 13, 2011)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The proof was sufficient to support defendant's conviction for first degree felony murder committed during the perpetration of a robbery, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-202 (2007), as defendant admitted that he took the victim's car, a witness testified that defendant acted alone in attacking the victim, and all of the medical testimony reflected that the victim died as a result of the injuries sustained during the attack; [2]-Defendant's challenge to the constitutionality of the death penalty for felony murder was rejected; [3]-Defendant's sentence of death was not disproportionate, as the evidence was sufficient for the jury to conclude that he struck repeated blows to the elderly victim, who suffered three separate skull fractures and broken ribs, in the process of stealing the victim's car, and the victim died as a result of these injuries.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

35 of 1427 DOCUMENTS



Lovlace v. Copley


No. M2011-00170-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


418 S.W.3d 1; 2013 Tenn. LEXIS 718


February 7, 2013, Session 
September 6, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Reversed; Judgment of the Trial Court Reinstated in Part and Vacated in Part. Appeal from the Chancery Court for Hickman County. No. 06-128-C. Robbie T. Beal, Judge.
Lovlace v. Copley, 2012 Tenn. App. LEXIS 74 (Tenn. Ct. App., Feb. 3, 2012)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Reversed; Judgment of the Trial Court Reinstated in Part and Vacated in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Tennessee Supreme Court concluded that the Adoption Statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-1-121(f), and the Grandparent Visitation Statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-6-306(d), do not conflict as the Grandparent Visitation Statute is more specific and clearly and unambiguously carves out a narrow, limited exception, in the case of grandparent visitation and stepparent adoption, to the more general rule stated in the Adoption Statute; [2]-An appellate court erred by reversing a judgment granting grandparent visitation because they had standing as they met the definition of a grandparent under Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-6-306(e) and the adoption of the child did not extinguish their previous visitation rights; [3]-The definition of grandparent under Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-6-306(e) includes two categories that do not require proof of a biological relationship with the child.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the appellate court reversed; judgment of the trial court reinstated, in part, and vacated, in part.

Mansell v. Bridgestone Firestone N. Am. Tire


No. M2012-02394-WC-R3-WC


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


417 S.W.3d 393; 2013 Tenn. LEXIS 645


May 1, 2013, Session Heard at Knoxville 
August 20, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. Sup. Ct. R. 51, § 2; Judgment of the Trial Court Reversed in Part; Affirmed and Modified in Part; Case Remanded to the Circuit Court for Smith County. Direct Appeal from the Circuit Court for Smith County. No. 2010CV36. John D. Wootten, Jr., Judge.
Mansell v. Bridgestone Firestone N. Am. Tire, LLC, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 766 (Tenn., Aug. 25, 2011)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court Reversed in Part; Affirmed and Modified in Part; Case Remanded to the Circuit Court for Smith County.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-204(d)(5) (2008 & Supp. 2012), presuming a medical impairment rating physician's rating was accurate unless rebutted by clear and convincing evidence, was not limited to Department of Labor and Workforce Development proceedings because no authority so limited it; [2]-it did not offend separation of powers, under Tenn. Const. art. II, §§ 1 and 2, because it did not impermissibly conflict with Tenn. R. Evid. 702, nor did a limit on a court's ability to appoint an expert impermissibly conflict with Tenn. R. Evid. 706; [3]-it did not violate procedural due process because it created no permanent irrebuttable presumption; [4]-it did not violate substantive due process because it legitimately exercised legislative power; [5]-the presumption was not rebutted because no such evidence was offered, and erroneous differences in qualifications were relied on.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed in part, affirmed and modified in part.

 

37 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Pratcher v. Methodist Healthcare Memphis Hosps.


No. W2011-01576-SC-S09-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


407 S.W.3d 727; 2013 Tenn. LEXIS 594


November 8, 2012, Session Heard at Memphis 
June 28, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 9 Interlocutory Appeal; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed; Case Remanded to the Circuit Court. Appeal by Permission from the Circuit Court for Shelby County. No. CT-0070011-00. Donna M. Fields, Judge.
Pratcher v. Methodist Healthcare-Memphis Hosps., 2011 Tenn. App. LEXIS 451 (Tenn. Ct. App., Aug. 19, 2011)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed; Case Remanded to the Circuit Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) that denied its motions to dismiss the case based on the statute of repose in Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-26-116(a)(3) (2012), and to amend its answer to add the statute as an affirmative defense.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff husband took his wife, who was 36 weeks pregnant, to the hospital after she vomited what appeared to be blood. When the resident obstetrician on call determined that the baby needed to be delivered by cesarean section, defendant nurse anesthetist was called away, and defendant owner/president declined to go to the hospital. Consequently, an anesthesiologist who did not work in obstetrics and was employed by defendant second employer, provided anesthesia for the surgery. Almost immediately after the first anesthetic drugs were administered to the wife, she began having respiratory distress and eventually died. The husband alleged that the employer was vicariously liable for the negligent acts of the nurse anesthetist and its owner/president. The state supreme court held that the running of § 29-26-116(a)(3) did not deprive the trial court of subject matter jurisdiction. The statute of repose was an affirmative defense under Rule 8.03. Therefore, as the employer did not raise the statute of repose as an affirmative defense at any time before trial, the trial court did not abuse its discretion by denying its motions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

38 of 1427 DOCUMENTS



Moncier v. Bd. of Prof'l Responsibility


No. E2012-00340-SC-R3-BP


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


406 S.W.3d 139; 2013 Tenn. LEXIS 491


January 3, 2013, Session 
May 24, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. Sup. Ct. R. 9, § 24.3 Direct Appeal; Judgment of the Board Panel Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Board of Professional Responsibility Panel. No. 2011-2058-2-NJ(24).
United States v. Vassar, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 7878 (E.D. Tenn., Jan. 6, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Board Panel Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney was suspended from the practice of law and was assessed costs associated with the proceedings that resulted in his suspension pursuant to Tenn. Sup. Ct. R. 9, § 24.3. The attorney filed a petition for judicial review pursuant to Tenn. R. Sup. Ct. Rule 9, §§ 24.3 and 1.3. The attorney appealed the denial of relief by a Tennessee Board of Professional Responsibility (Board) hearing panel.


OVERVIEW: The state's highest court held that Rule 9, § 24.3 was not unconstitutionally vague under Tenn. Const. art. I, § 8 and the Fourteenth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The attorney's state and federal due process rights were not violated. The attorney received notice and had an opportunity to be heard before costs were assessed against him. He also received extensive post-assessment process. The Board satisfied Rule 9, § 24.3. The state's highest court had subject matter jurisdiction to include an assessment of costs in the order of enforcement, and was not divested of subject matter jurisdiction due to pending appeals. Attorneys in disciplinary proceedings were not entitled to the same due process rights afforded criminal defendants. Tennessee's disciplinary processes satisfied due process. Disciplinary Counsel and staff of the Board did not deprive the attorney of counsel of his choosing. The panel had authority to adjudicate the attorney's petition, even though its members had not taken an oath under Tenn. Const. art. X, § 1. The Tennessee Code of Judicial Conduct did not apply to panel members. The attorney's motion for recusal and discovery requests were properly denied.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

39 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Lake v. Memphis Landsmen, LLC


No. W2011-00660-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


405 S.W.3d 47; 2013 Tenn. LEXIS 434; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P19,098


November 7, 2012, Session 
May 3, 2013, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at, Remanded by Lake v. Memphis Landsmen, LLC, 2014 Tenn. App. LEXIS 128 (Tenn. Ct. App., Mar. 7, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Reversed; Case Remanded to the Court of Appeals. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals, Western Section Circuit Court for Shelby County. No. CT00609400. John R. McCarroll, Jr., Judge.
Lake v. Memphis Landsmen, L.L.C., 2011 Tenn. App. LEXIS 568 (Tenn. Ct. App., Oct. 21, 2011)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Reversed; Case Remanded to the Court of Appeals.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a passenger and his wife, filed an action against defendants, a bus owner, a bus manufacturer, and a bus window manufacturer. They challenged a judgment of the Court of Appeals (Tennessee), which held that Federal Motor Vehicle Safety Standards (FMVSS) 205 and 208, 49 C.F.R. §§ 571.205 and 571.208, preempted their claims based on the lack of passenger seatbelts on a bus and the material used in the window glass of the bus.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court held that plaintiffs' claims were not preempted by federal law. FMVSS 208 did not preempt plaintiffs' claim based on defendants' failure to provide passenger seatbelts. The history of seatbelt regulation under FMVSS 208, the National Highway Traffic Safety Administration's (NHTSA) explanation of its objectives, and its views on the preemptive effect of the regulation compelled the conclusion that FMVSS 208 did not preempt plaintiffs' claim premised on the lack of passenger seatbelts. FMVSS 205 did not preempt that portion of plaintiffs' claim based upon the use of tempered glass side windows. There was no indication that the primary concern raised by defendants, the increased risk of impact neck injuries associated with laminated glass, motivated NHTSA's decision to give manufacturers the option of installing side windows made of tempered glass rather than requiring laminated glass. The bus did not have passenger seatbelts. Thus, the concern that laminated glass could be more dangerous for belted passengers did not apply, and plaintiffs' claim did not stand as an obstacle to the regulatory objective of reducing injuries caused by impact with glazing surfaces.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the judgment and remanded the case to the court of appeals to decide the remaining issues raised.

State v. Johnson


No. E2010-00172-SC-DDT-DD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


401 S.W.3d 1; 2013 Tenn. LEXIS 355


January 3, 2013, Session 
April 19, 2013, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Johnson v. Tennessee, 2013 U.S. LEXIS 7883 (U.S., Nov. 4, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(a)(1); Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Automatic Appeal from the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Sullivan County. No. S50059. R. Jerry Beck, Judge.
State v. Johnson, 2012 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 132 (Tenn. Crim. App., Mar. 5, 2012)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to death. The Tennessee Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in ruling that he made a knowing and voluntary waiver of his right to present mitigation evidence under U.S. Const. amend. VIII. The supreme court disagreed. The trial court complied with both the letter and spirit of the Zagorski inquiry. The trial court informed defendant of his right to present mitigation evidence and questioned him to determine whether he understood his rights and the importance of presenting mitigation evidence. The trial court called defendant to make a special appearance to testify about his decision to waive mitigation evidence. The trial court confirmed that defendant and counsel discussed the importance of mitigating evidence. The trial court also asked defendant to define mitigating circumstances and describe how he envisioned the jury would factor that evidence into its decision. Finally, the trial court considered defendant's explanation for waiving the evidence. When defendant announced his desire to offer non-mental health mitigation evidence, the trial court again discussed with him the specific parameters of the evidence he wished to present.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Whitehead v. State


No. W2010-00784-SC-R11-PC


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


402 S.W.3d 615; 2013 Tenn. LEXIS 310


October 2, 2012, Session in Nashville 
March 21, 2013, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 31, 2014.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Reversed. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 03-04835. James C. Beasley, Jr., Judge.
Whitehead v. State, 2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 699 (Tenn. Crim. App., Sept. 7, 2011)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sought post-conviction relief after the deadline contained in the Post-Conviction Procedure Act of 1995, Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-102(a) (2012), had passed because his former attorney provided him the wrong deadline date and failed to give the prisoner his legal files until after the deadline passed. He challenged a judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed the dismissal of his petition as untimely.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court held that the statute of limitations was tolled. The prisoner was effectively abandoned by his appellate attorney after his petition for writ of certiorari was filed in the United States Supreme Court. That abandonment impeded the prisoner's otherwise diligent efforts to file a timely post-conviction petition. He was pursuing his rights diligently. Nothing in the record indicated that the prisoner was aware that the United States Supreme Court had denied his petition for certiorari until he received a misleading letter from his appellate lawyer five months after the fact. That letter also belatedly alerted the prisoner to the possibility of post-conviction relief. The prisoner did not already possess the files he needed, and the files his lawyer held contained critical information for his post-conviction petition. The lawyer's unreasonable delay in sending the prisoner his files, exacerbated by the lawyer's erroneous deadline and the delay in notifying the prisoner that his direct appeals were exhausted and that the attorney-client relationship had ended, constituted an objective factor, an impediment that could not be fairly attributed to the prisoner.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the decision of the court of criminal appeals and remanded the case to the trial court to proceed with the prisoner's petition for post-conviction relief.

Keen v. State


No. W2011-00789-SC-R11-PD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


398 S.W.3d 594; 2012 Tenn. LEXIS 932


May 31, 2012, Session Heard at Lipscomb University1


1 Oral argument was presented on the campus of Lipscomb University in Nashville, Davidson County, Tennessee, as a part of the Girls State Supreme Court Advancing Legal Education for Students (S.C.A.L.E.S.) project.

 
December 20, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Keen v. Tennessee, 134 S. Ct. 176, 187 L. Ed. 2d 120, 2013 U.S. LEXIS 7234 (U.S., Oct. 7, 2013)
Request denied by Keen v. State, 2017 Tenn. LEXIS 346 (Tenn., May 24, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. P25157. Chris Craft, Judge.
Keen v. State, 2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 972 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 29, 2011)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate's motion to reopen his post-conviction petition on the ground that he possessed new scientific evidence of his actual innocence was denied. The Tennessee Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed the denial. The inmate was granted permission to appeal to the state's highest court.


OVERVIEW: The state's highest court held that a motion to reopen was the proper vehicle for bringing the inmate's claims. The inmate's motion was filed within one year of Coleman for Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-117(a)(1) purposes. However, Coleman did not establish a new retroactive rule for proving an intellectual disability in Tennessee under the Eighth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. VIII or Tenn. Const. art. I, § 16. Coleman concerned the interpretation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-203 (2010), and held that the courts could consider factors other than raw test scores in determining intellectual disability. To qualify as actually innocent under § 40-30-117(a)(2), the inmate had to show actual innocence of the underlying crimes. There was no separate offense in Tennessee for capital murder, and the inmate had pled guilty to first degree murder. The death penalty was a sentencing consideration, rather than an independent offense. To reopen post-conviction proceedings under § 40-30-117(a)(2) (2006), the inmate had to present scientific evidence that he was actually innocent of the offense. The claim that the inmate was ineligible for the death penalty did not qualify as an actual innocence claim.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the post-conviction court and the appellate court were affirmed.

State v. Bise


No. E2011-00005-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


380 S.W.3d 682; 2012 Tenn. LEXIS 645


May 9, 2012, Session 
September 26, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Reversed. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals. Circuit Court for Greene County. No. 09CR353. John F. Dugger, Jr., Judge.
State v. Bise, 2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 715 (Tenn. Crim. App., Sept. 15, 2011)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of facilitation of aggravated burglary and two counts of theft of property. After finding the presence of one enhancement factor, the trial court imposed concurrent three-year sentences for each offense. Defendant appealed. The Tennessee Court of Criminal Appeals found that the enhancement factor did not apply and reduced each of the sentences to two years. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant waited in her truck while her son and an accomplice burglarized the victim's home. The trial court applied the enhancement factor of Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-114(10)--that defendant committed a crime when the risk to human life was high, as the homeowner could have arrived at any time and placed the perpetrators at risk. The intermediate appellate court reduced the sentences on grounds the trial court improperly applied this enhancement factor. The high court held that under the 2005 amendments to the Tennessee Criminal Sentencing Reform Act of 1989, even if a trial court improperly applied an enhancement factor, it did not abuse its discretion if it did not increase the sentence beyond the minimum on the basis of that factor. It adopted an abuse of discretion standard of review, granting a presumption of reasonableness to within-range sentencing decisions that reflected a proper application of the purposes and principles of the Act. Though the trial court relied on an erroneous enhancement factor, the sentence it imposed was supported by the reasons it articulated in the record, including the need for deterrence; thus, the sentence should not have been reduced.


OUTCOME: The high court reversed the intermediate appellate court's sentence modification and reinstated the sentence the trial court imposed.

State v. Donaldson


No. M2010-00690-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


380 S.W.3d 86; 2012 Tenn. LEXIS 582


June 14, 2012, Session 
August 24, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals is Reversed; Remanded to the Criminal Court for Davidson County. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals, Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2009C2849. Cheryl A. Blackburn, Judge.
State v. Donaldson, 2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 717 (Tenn. Crim. App., Sept. 15, 2011)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals is Reversed; Remanded to the Criminal Court for Davidson County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged a judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed the trial court's order sustaining defendant's motion to suppress cocaine a police officer observed in his vehicle. The officer stopped defendant for a traffic violation and observed the cocaine when he ordered defendant out of his vehicle to sign the citation pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-10-207 (2008).


OVERVIEW: The supreme court held that the trial court erroneously ruled that the officer had concluded the stop by handing defendant his driver's license before removing him from the car. The officer was entitled to remove defendant from the vehicle for a short period of time after making the traffic stop. The officer described the stop of defendant as "normal." Nothing in the record indicated that the stop lasted more than five minutes. The officer, who was the only witness at the hearing, testified that he had not returned the driver's license before asking defendant to step outside the vehicle, and upon further inquiry, the trial court confirmed the sequence of events as related by the officer. Neither the original order of suppression nor the order denying the State's motion to reconsider questioned the officer's credibility. The traffic stop had not been completed at the time defendant was asked to step out of his vehicle. The balance of the competing interests favored the safety of the officer over the minimal intrusion to an individual directed to step outside of his vehicle after a valid traffic stop. That rationale applied under the Fourth Amendment and Tenn. Const. art. I, § 7.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the order of suppression and remanded the case to the trial court for trial.

Hooker v. Haslam


No. M2012-01318-SC-RDM-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


393 S.W.3d 156; 2012 Tenn. LEXIS 719



July 27, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 12C-735.
Hooker v. Haslam, 382 S.W.3d 358, 2012 Tenn. App. LEXIS 511 (Tenn. Ct. App., 2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An alleged candidate sued defendants, the heads of the branches of state government and an appellate court judge (collectively, the State), challenging the judge's appointment and an impending retention election. The trial court dismissed the case. The candidate appealed to the Tennessee Court of Appeals. He also requested the high court to review the case under Tenn. Code Ann. 16-3-201(d)(1) (Supp. 2011), and that its members recuse themselves.


OVERVIEW: The alleged candidate contended that the Tennessee Plan, Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 17-4-101 through 17-4-119 (2009), which provided for the selection and evaluation of state appellate judges, was unconstitutional. He argued that the economic interests of the members of the high court in their respective offices required their disqualification under Tenn. Const. art. VI, § 11. The high court held that although the principle of stare decisis appeared to govern the circumstances, and the State made a persuasive argument that res judicata barred the candidate's claims, under former Tenn. Sup. Ct. R. 10, Canon 3(E), the high court's participation in the appeal had to be measured against an objective standard for recusal. Under Tenn. Const. art. VI, § 7, members of the high court had a protected interest in maintaining their salaries during the course of their terms. As there was an appearance of the members' economic interest in their own compensation, and as the legislature, pursuant to Tenn. Const. art. VI, § 11, had authorized both the Governor and chief justice to designate temporary judges, recusal was appropriate under the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The members of the high court recused themselves and certified to the Governor the need for the appointment of a special supreme court.

In re Estate of Trigg


No. M2009-02107-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


368 S.W.3d 483; 2012 Tenn. LEXIS 379


October 6, 2011, Session 
May 30, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals, Middle Section, Circuit Court for Putnam County. No. 08N0305. John J. Maddux, Jr., Judge.
In re Estate of Ardell Hamilton Trigg, 2011 Tenn. App. LEXIS 53 (Tenn. Ct. App., Feb. 9, 2011)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a will was admitted to probate, the Bureau of TennCare filed a claim against the estate, seeking reimbursement for services provided through the TennCare program. The personal representative filed an exception to the claim. The probate court upheld the claim, but the circuit court reversed. The Court of Appeals, Middle Section (Tennessee) held that the circuit court lacked jurisdiction, and vacated the judgment. The estate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The decedent left behind a small estate consisting of some personal property and a house. TennCare sought to recover a sum for nursing home and long-term care services. The circuit court lacked subject matter jurisdiction under Tenn. Code Ann. § 30-2-609(b)(2) because the decision did not involve the final settlement of the estate by the personal representative. Instead, the estate was only entitled to appeal to the court of appeals under with Tenn. Code Ann. § 30-2-315(b). While the court of appeals correctly found that the estate appealed the probate court's decision to the wrong court, it should not have summarily dismissed TennCare's appeal. It should have vacated the circuit court's judgment and remanded the case to the circuit court with directions to transfer the case to the court of appeals in accordance with Tenn. Code Ann. § 16-4-108(a)(2). Once the case was properly before it, the court of appeals could then have addressed the substantive issues raised by the parties. On the merits, under both 42 U.S.C.S. § 1396p and Tenn. Code Ann. § 71-5-116, TennCare was entitled to reach the decedent's assets to obtain reimbursement for services supplied through the TennCare program.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the court of appeals.

State v. Sexton


No. E2008-00292-SC-DDT-DD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


368 S.W.3d 371; 2012 Tenn. LEXIS 377


February 15, 2012, Session at Nashville 
May 29, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Corrected by State v. Sexton, 2012 Tenn. LEXIS 739 (Tenn., May 29, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(a)(1); Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part. Automatic Appeal from the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Scott County. No. 7685. E. Shayne Sexton, Judge.
State v. Sexton, 2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1035 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 7, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial, defendant was convicted of two counts of first degree murder (Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-202 (1997)) and was sentenced to death for each offense. He appealed; the Tennessee Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed. He sought further review.


OVERVIEW: A child of one of the victims had accused defendant of molesting her; he told three witnesses he killed the victims. He obtained a.22 rifle shortly before the murders; fragments from the bodies were consistent with a.22 bullet. The high court held the trial court erred in admitting evidence of defendant's sexual abuse the child to show motive; because of the inherent unreliability of a witness's recollections of the child's allegations of sexual abuse, defendant's commission of that crime was not proven by clear and convincing evidence. After an officer improperly referred to defendant's refusal to submit to a polygraph, the trial court erred in not providing curative instructions. The prosecutor made improper comments in the opening statement, during the guilt phase of the trial testimony, and in the closing arguments of the guilt and penalty phases. As evidence of defendant's guilt was overwhelming, the errors did not warrant reversal of the convictions. But because of the improper striking of jurors, the prejudicial error in the admission of evidence, and the improper comments by the prosecution, the verdicts imposing death sentences for each murder could not stand.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed but the verdicts imposing death sentences for each murder were set aside and the cases were remanded to the trial court for new sentencing hearings.

State v. Sexton

SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2012 Tenn. LEXIS 739
