PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(a)(1); Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part. Automatic Appeal from the Court of Criminal Appeals, Criminal Court for Scott County. No. 7685. E. Shayne Sexton, Judge.
State v. Sexton, 368 S.W.3d 371, 2012 Tenn. LEXIS 377 (Tenn., 2012)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the trial court of two counts of first degree murder, in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-202 (1997). Defendant was sentenced to death for each offense as the jury found the aggravating circumstance under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204(i)(6) (1997 & Supp. 1999). The Court of Criminal Appeals of Tennessee affirmed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victims, husband and wife, were shot to death as they slept in their home. The murders took place days after the minor daughter of one of the victims reported to authorities that she had been sexually abused by defendant, her stepfather. On appeal, the court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretionary authority by refusing to change the venue of the trial. However, the court erred by improperly striking jurors, by admitting evidence of a prior claim of child sex abuse, and by allowing references to defendant's refusal to submit to a polygraph examination. Further, several instances of prosecutorial misconduct occurred during the opening statement and during the final arguments of both the guilt and penalty phases of the trial. Because, however, defendant admitted to at least three witnesses that he committed the murders and the evidence of guilt was otherwise overwhelming, the errors had no effect on the verdicts rendered at the conclusion of the guilt phase of the trial. Nevertheless, because certain of the inadmissible evidence was particularly inflammatory and the prosecution made several inappropriate comments, the sentences of death had to be set aside.


OUTCOME: The intermediate appellate court was affirmed in part as to the guilty verdicts for the first degree murders and reversed in part as to the imposition of the death sentences for the murders. The cause was remanded to the trial court for new sentencing hearings.

Lojac Enters. v. Kanipe


No. M2011-01525-WC-R3-WC


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, SPECIAL WORKERS' COMPENSATION APPEALS PANEL, AT NASHVILLE


2012 Tenn. LEXIS 308


April 9, 2012, Mailed 
May 10, 2012, Filed


NOTICE: CONSULT THE TENNESSEE SUPREME COURT RULES FOR CITATION OF UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Adopted by, Affirmed by Lojac Enters. v. Kanipe, 2012 Tenn. LEXIS 307 (Tenn., May 10, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] 
Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-225(e) (2008) Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 10 C 3001. Amanda McClendon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer filed an action to reconsider appellee employee's benefits. The employee filed a motion to dismiss, contending that Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-241(d)(1)(B)(iv) (2008) did not permit an employer to file a reconsideration action. The employer challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), which granted the motion to dismiss and found that § 50-6-241 did not violate Tenn. Const. art. I, § 17.


OVERVIEW: The employee was injured while working for the employer. His workers' compensation claim was settled. As a part of his settlement, he retained a right of reconsideration pursuant to § 50-6-241(d)(1). The employer contended that § 50-6-241 permitted filing of a reconsideration action by an employer and that the statute was unconstitutional. The supreme court held that the trial court correctly held that § 50-6-241(d)(1)(B)(iv) did not permit an employer to file a reconsideration action. The language of § 50-6-241(d)(1)(B)(iv) unambiguously authorized only an employee to file a petition for reconsideration of a prior workers' compensation award or settlement. Because the rights and remedies afforded to both employees and employers by the workers' compensation statutes were adequate substitutes to common-law tort remedies and procedures, § 50-6-241 did not violate the Opens Courts Clause in Tenn. Const, art. I, § 17. It was undoubtedly rational to permit the employee alone to determine whether or not it was in his or her interest to litigate in pursuit of a potential remedy.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment.

Smith v. State


No. E2007-00719-SC-R11-PD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


357 S.W.3d 322; 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 1152


August 31, 2011, Session1


1 Oral argument in this case was heard at the Duncan School of Law, Lincoln Memorial University, in Knoxville, Tennessee.

 
December 19, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Smith v. Tenn., 2012 U.S. LEXIS 6925 (U.S., Oct. 1, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed in Part and Vacated in Part; Case Remanded to Post-Conviction Court. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Hamblen County. No. 99CR310. O. Duane Slone, Judge.
Smith v. State, 2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 793 (Tenn. Crim. App., Sept. 21, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed in Part and Vacated in Part; Case Remanded to Post-Conviction Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a judgment of the Tennessee Court of Criminal Appeals that affirmed the denial of his motion for post-conviction relief following his two convictions of first-degree felony murder and the imposition of the death penalty, arguing that he received ineffective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: After reviewing the facts of the case and applying Strickland and its progeny, the court held that defendant was denied the right to a fair trial because of counsel's errors. The failure of defense counsel to adequately investigate and support a motion for the recusal of the presiding trial judge resulted in prejudice to defendant, and defendant was denied the right to a fair trial before an impartial tribunal. The potential injury to the judicial process due to the appearance of impropriety and unfair lack of impartiality by a judge imposing a death sentence was too great to allow the sentence of death to stand. The judge's former role as the prosecutor of defendant on other criminal charges at the same time as his trial for murder, multiple and regular instances of communication between the judge and other prosecutors regarding defendant's criminal cases, and the judge's acquisition of defendant's statement regarding his involvement in the murders compelled a conclusion that Strickland prejudice had been established by, among other things, operation of the denial of due process and the specter of potential unfairness.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and life sentence for one murder were affirmed. His conviction for the second murder was affirmed, but his death sentence was vacated, and the case was remanded for a determination of whether defendant met the criteria of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-203(a) for intellectual impairment under the correct legal standard.

Webb v. Nashville Area Habitat for Humanity, Inc.


No. M2009-01552-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


346 S.W.3d 422; 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 623; 32 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1124


February 3, 2011, Session 
July 21, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals, Middle Section Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 09C-1221. Barbara N. Haynes, Judge.
Webb v. Nashville Area Habitat for Humanity, Inc., 2010 Tenn. App. LEXIS 273 (Tenn. Ct. App., Apr. 16, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee employee filed a retaliatory discharge action against appellant employer under the Tennessee Public Protection Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-1-304 (2008 & Supp. 2010) and the common law. The trial court granted the employer's motion to dismiss for failure to state a claim under Tenn. R. Civ. P. 12.02(6). The employee appealed. The Court of Appeals, Middle Section (Tennessee), vacated the trial court's judgment. The employer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee's amended complaint alleged that she was terminated by the employer for her complaints regarding, and her unwillingness to implement, participate in or remain silent about, discriminatory and illegal policies that the employer's management requested staff members to implement. The supreme court declined to adopt the new Twombly/Iqbal plausibility pleading standard and followed the notice pleading regime. Construing the complaint liberally, presuming all factual allegations to be true and giving the employee the benefit of all reasonable inferences, it was not apparent from the face of the amended complaint that the employee could have proven no set of facts in support of the claim that would have entitled her to relief. The amended complaint specifically referred to the statute upon which the employee was relying to state her claim, Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-1-304, and thus comported with Tenn. R. Civ. P. 8.05(1). The amended complaint, while not a model of pleading, provided the employer with sufficient notice of the claims alleged and sufficiently pleaded a legal cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

In re Bell


No. M2010-01447-SC-R3-CJ


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


344 S.W.3d 304; 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 577

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. Code Ann. § 17-5-310(a) (2009) Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Court of the Judiciary Affirmed in Part and Affirmed as to Sanctions. Direct Appeal from the Court of the Judiciary. No. 08-3508.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of the Judiciary Affirmed in Part and Affirmed as to Sanctions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judge sought review of a decision from appellee, the Court of the Judiciary (Tennessee), which held that the judge violated various Canons of the Tennessee Code of Judicial Conduct. Sanctions that included a suspension were imposed.


OVERVIEW: Formal charges were filed against the judge pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 17-5-304(d)(2)(A) (2009), arising from a complaint by a pro se personal injury litigant who had a case before the judge. The Court of the Judiciary found that the judge violated Tenn. Sup. Ct. R. 10, Canon 3(B)(7), (8), (E)(1), and 2(A) by taking nine months to decide a personal injury action, rehearing the case without disclosing to a new party that he had made findings against the new party as to liability and damages, and contacting the self-represented complainant, through an attorney, while the case was still pending before him. The Court of the Judiciary imposed sanctions upon consideration of the factors under Tenn. Code Ann. § 17-5-301(i) (2009). On appeal, the court found clear and convincing evidence under Tenn. Code Ann. § 17-5-308(d) (2009) to support the findings that the judge committed violations with respect to the delay and the ex parte communication. The judge was not required to disqualify himself merely because he made a prior decision in the case. Under a de novo review pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 17-5-310(b)(1), the court agreed with the sanctions imposed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of the judiciary as to the violations resulting from the delay and ex parte communications. It reversed the decision regarding the violation for failure to disclose a prior decision. It also affirmed the judgment as to the sanctions imposed.

 

53 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Coleman v. State


No. W2007-02767-SC-R11-PD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


341 S.W.3d 221; 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 319


November 3, 2010, Session 
April 11, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed in Part and Vacated in Part. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals, Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. P-11326. W. Mark Ward, Judge.
Coleman v. State, 2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 36 (Tenn. Crim. App., Jan. 13, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed in Part and Vacated in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of the decision of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed the trial court's dismissal of his motion to reopen his postconviction petition.


OVERVIEW: The inmate's appeal involved the role of expert testimony in proceedings to determine whether he was intellectually disabled and thus barred from being executed under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-203 (2010). The inmate had filed a motion to reopen his postconviction proceedings on the ground that he was intellectually disabled at the time he committed the crime, the trial court dismissed the motion, and the appellate court affirmed. The supreme court found that § 39-13-203(a)(1) did not require that raw scores on I.Q. tests be accepted at their face value and that the courts could consider competent expert testimony showing that a test score did not accurately reflect a person's functional I.Q. or that the raw I.Q. test score was artificially inflated or deflated. Thus, categorically excluding expert testimony was erroneous. However, the inmate's claim involving the ineffective assistance of his trial counsel was barred.


OUTCOME: The case was affirmed in part, vacated in part, and remanded. On remand, inmate and the State were free to present additional evidence regarding whether the inmate met the definition of intellectual disability under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-203(a) (2010).

State v. Odom


No. W2008-02464-SC-DDT-DD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT MEMPHIS


336 S.W.3d 541; 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 192


November 4, 2010, Session 
March 3, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended August 6, 2011.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Odom v. Tenn., 2011 U.S. LEXIS 7329 (U.S., Oct. 11, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(a)(1); Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals is Affirmed. Automatic Appeal from the Court of Criminal Appeals, Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 91-07049. Chris Craft, Judge.
State v. Odom, 2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 305 (Tenn. Crim. App., Apr. 13, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder in the perpetration of rape. In the penalty phase of the trial, the jury imposed a sentence of death. The Tennessee Court of Appeals affirmed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the imposition of the death penalty was improper under Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 39-13-206 and 39-13-204. The court of appeals disagreed. The State proved that defendant had murdered a person in 1978. The jury was presented with the judgment of conviction for that crime. The State also presented evidence that defendant murdered the victim in the instant case during a robbery. The State submitted photographic and testimonial evidence describing the nature and circumstances of the crime, which allowed the jury to assess the weight to be given the proffered aggravating circumstances. In mitigation, the defense presented defendant's personal history, which outlined his abandonment by his birth parents and separation from his siblings at a young age. The jury also heard evidence concerning defendant's almost spotless record while incarcerated. The jury also heard from an expert who opined that defendant had the capacity to do well in the prison environment. The State rebutted that evidence by describing defendant's escape from prison and his prior theft and robbery convictions, both of which were committed after his escape.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Hooker


No. M2009-01498-SC-OT-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


340 S.W.3d 389; 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 174



February 25, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
BPR Docket No. 2005P-1519-5-SG.
Hooker v. Crawford, 2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 30 (Tenn. Ct. App., Jan. 17, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An attorney filed a motion requesting the court set aside an order directing the Clerk of the Appellate Courts to decline to accept any of his further filings in the case and to rescind its order enforcing the suspension of his license to practice law for 30 days. The attorney also requested that all the members of the Supreme Court of Tennessee, at Nashville recuse themselves due to prejudice.


OVERVIEW: For nearly two decades, the attorney filed a series of lawsuits in the federal and state courts challenging the financing of elections by officials running for local, state, and federal office. When those actions met with no success, the attorney began challenging the authority of the state appellate courts to hear and decide his claims, alleging the judges were not validly elected. When those challenges failed, he accused the judges who rejected his claims of engaging in unethical and criminal misconduct. The supreme court first concluded that there was no reasonable ground for disqualification of any of the members of the court; among other things, no reasonable person familiar with the practice of law could conclude that the members of the court had any personal interest in the attorney's law license. In addition, the election of a judge was not an adequate basis for disqualification. While supreme court declined to set aside the order directing the Clerk to decline further filings from the attorney, the papers filed prior that order were not effected. Finally, the supreme court concluded that the issue of the attorney's suspension was not in a posture that permitted review.


OUTCOME: The Clerk was directed to accept and file a specified motion filed by the attorney. The attorney's motion for recusal was denied. The attorney was ordered to provide the Clerk with certified copies of the papers he and the Board of Professional Responsibility filed upon seeking judicial review and, within 45 days, file a brief.

State v. Dorantes


No. M2007-01918-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


331 S.W.3d 370; 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 8


October 7, 2010, Session Heard at Centerville 1


1 Oral argument was heard in this case on October 7, 2010, in Centerville, Hickman County, Tennessee, as part of this Court's S.C.A.L.E.S. (Supreme Court Advancing Legal Education for Students) project.

 
January 25, 2011, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Reversed in Part and Affirmed in Part. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2006-D-3184. Steve R. Dozier, Judge.
State v. Dorantes, 2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 965 (Tenn. Crim. App., Nov. 30, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Reversed in Part and Affirmed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of aggravated child abuse, in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-15-402 (Supp. 2002), and felony murder by aggravated child abuse, in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-202(a)(2) (Supp. 1998). Defendant appealed. The Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee) reversed the conviction for aggravated child abuse, but upheld the felony murder conviction. Both the State and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The General Assembly chose to provide two separate courses of conduct, aggravated child abuse and aggravated child neglect, upon which the felony murder could have been predicated. Under the doctrine of in loco parentis, defendant's failure to seek medical assistance for the victim's injuries may have supported convictions for aggravated child neglect and felony murder by aggravated child neglect, but the State was precluded from charging him with those particular crimes by the terms of an extradition agreement and the doctrine of specialty. Nonetheless, the proof showed that defendant knowingly treated the child in such a manner as to inflict injury, either as principal or as one criminally responsible for the conduct of another. The evidence, even though entirely circumstantial, was sufficient to support the jury's finding of guilt beyond a reasonable doubt of each of the offenses charged. The autopsy report, photographs of the injuries, and defendant's flight from Louisiana and hiding out for three years were especially probative. Further, the trial court's charge to the jury was adequate, and its refusal to supplement the pattern instruction did not constitute reversible error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction for felony murder. It reversed the court of criminal appeals' judgment with regard to the charge of aggravated child abuse, and reinstated defendant's conviction. The sentences imposed by the trial court of life and twenty-two years, respectively, were affirmed.

Blue Bell Creameries, LP v. Roberts


No. M2009-00255-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


333 S.W.3d 59; 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 6; 74 A.L.R.6th 613


June 3, 2010, Session 
January 24, 2011, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Blue Bell Creameries v. Roberts, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 4839 (U.S., June 27, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Reversed; Summary Judgment Granted; Case Remanded. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals, Middle Section Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 06-414-III. Ellen H. Lyle, Chancellor.
Blue Bell Creameries, L.P. v. Chumley, 2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 655 (Tenn. Ct. App., Sept. 29, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Reversed; Summary Judgment Granted; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A taxpayer limited partnership sought a refund and challenged the validity of an excise tax assessment on capital gains from a one-time stock transaction. The trial court granted summary judgment to the taxpayer. The Court of Appeals (Tennessee) affirmed the judgment. The Tennessee Department of Revenue appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Department's assessment of excise tax on the taxpayer's capital gains from the stock transaction and reorganization between the taxpayer and its holding company was permissible pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-4-2004 (Supp. 2000) and the United States Constitution. The earnings at issue were from a one-time, extraordinary transaction. The capital gains did not qualify as business earnings under the transactional test because the earnings did not arise from transactions or activity in the regular course of the taxpayer's ice cream business. However, the capital gains were business earnings pursuant to the functional test provided in § 67-4-2004(1) because the taxpayer's acquisition and sale of the stock contributed materially to the production of business earnings arising from the sale of ice cream. Additionally, the tax assessment was constitutional pursuant to the unitary business principle. The taxpayer and the Department both filed motions for summary judgment. There was no genuine issue of material fact. Accordingly, summary judgment should have been entered in favor of the Department, and not in favor of the taxpayer.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals. It granted summary judgment in favor of the Department and remanded the matter to the trial court to determine the amount of excise tax related to the taxpayer's capital gains.

Fannon v. City of Lafollette


No. E2008-01616-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


329 S.W.3d 418; 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 1207


September 2, 2010, Session 
December 21, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part and Remanded. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals Circuit Court for Campbell County. No. 13947. John D. McAfee, Judge.
Fannon v. City of Lafollette, 2010 Tenn. App. LEXIS 5 (Tenn. Ct. App., Jan. 11, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An appeal was permitted of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Tennessee) that plaintiff LaFollette City Council member had standing as a taxpayer, rather than in his official capacity, to seek a declaratory judgment under the Tennessee Open Meetings Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 8-44-101 to -111 (2002), but reversed an award of attorney fees to him in his action against defendants that included the City of LaFollette and three other Council members.


OVERVIEW: After the trial court temporarily halted budget amendments to support city employee pay raises agreed to in a meeting about which the member filed suit under the Open Meetings Act, the Council met again to approve the pay raises following correct procedure. The trial court then dismissed the member's claim as moot but awarded him fees and costs. On review of the Court of Appeals decision, the court held that the member had standing and was a prevailing party but was not entitled to recover attorney's fees in addition to costs. He failed to demonstrate standing as a taxpayer because there was no indication that he had demanded remedial measures prior to filing suit. However, a threshold showing of an Open Meetings Act violation was sufficient to confer standing to any citizen and lack of public notice in this case was not refuted. While the trial court did not address whether the Act had been violated, its temporary order based on a finding of a violation of the City Charter resulted in a change of the status quo and the member thus was a prevailing party entitled under the American Rule and Tenn. R. Civ. P. 54.04(2) to costs but not attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the judgment of the court of appeals and remanded the cause to the trial court for entry of an order granting the member costs included in the bill of costs prepared by clerk and discretionary costs.

OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment was affirmed and the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with the supreme court's opinion.

State v. Henretta


No. E2007-01750-SC-DDT-DD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


325 S.W.3d 112; 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 888


May 4, 2010, Session 
September 30, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Henretta v. Tennessee, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 2671 (U.S., Apr. 4, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(a)(1) Automatic Appeal. Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Automatic Appeal from the Court of Criminal Appeals. Criminal Court for Bradley County. No. 97-334. R. Steven Bebb, Judge.
State v. Henretta, 2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1086 (Tenn. Crim. App., Apr. 14, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of premeditated murder, felony murder, two counts of robbery with a deadly weapon, two counts of aggravated rape, and two counts of aggravated kidnapping. The trial court merged the premeditated murder and felony murder convictions into a single conviction for which the jury imposed a sentence of death. The Tennessee Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that his death sentence was disproportionate under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206. The supreme court disagreed. Defendant and his accomplice hid in the thrift store where the victim was working alone as a clerk and, after raping and robbing her, defendant cut her throat and killed her without provocation or justification. The victim offered no resistance to the offenses committed against her and was obviously helpless in the face of her assailants. Defendant was forty-five years of age at the time of the murder and had a prior criminal history of violent crimes, include convictions for rape and murder. Defendant had an unstable childhood, was of relatively low intelligence, and exhibited brain damage and dysfunction as a result of which he had an abnormally low ability to inhibit aggressive or violent urges. After being approached by law enforcement officers defendant was cooperative and confessed to the crime; however, he did not offer any information regarding his involvement in the murder during the more than five years between the time of the murder and the time of the meeting. The sentence of death was neither excessive nor disproportionate.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

61 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Elliott v. Cobb


No. W2009-00961-SC-S09-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


320 S.W.3d 246; 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 875


April 6, 2010, Session 
September 23, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 9 Interlocutory Appeal; Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed; Case Remanded to the Circuit Court for Madison County. Interlocutory Appeal from the Circuit Court for Madison County. No. C-05-436. Donald H. Allen, Judge.
Elliott v. Cobb, 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 787 (Tenn., Nov. 23, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed; Case Remanded to the Circuit Court for Madison County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff patient's medical malpractice action defendant surgeon, the trial court granted the surgeon's motion in limine and prohibited the patient from making any reference or suggestion during the trial to any specific sum for any element of non-economic damages or the ultimate monetary worth of the action. The Court of Appeals of Tennessee affirmed. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that the plain language of Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-26-117 (2000) prohibited the patient from disclosing the amount of damages requested in her pleading, but did not preclude her from arguing or suggesting monetary amounts for non-economic damages to jurors at trial, and therefore the trial court erred by granting the surgeon's motion in limine. The court further held that § 29-26-117 and Tenn. Code Ann. § 20-9-304 (2009) were not in conflict, and that the statutory scheme allowed a plaintiff to argue or suggest a monetary value to be placed on non-economic damages such as pain and suffering and to make an argument concerning the ultimate monetary worth of his or her action, but precluded either party from disclosing the amount of the ad damnum clause in the plaintiff's complaint. Had the legislature intended to repeal § 20-9-304 in medical malpractice cases, it could have done so as it did with Tenn. Code Ann. § 20-9-302 but it did not.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

State v. Jordan


No. W2007-01272-SC-DDT-DD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


325 S.W.3d 1; 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 874



September 22, 2010, Filed

Post-conviction relief denied at Jordan v. State, 2016 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 772 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 14, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(a)(1); Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Court of Criminal Appeals. Circuit Court for Madison County. No. 05-431. Roy B. Morgan, Jr., Judge.
State v. Jordan, 2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 455 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 9, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed his convictions and sentences for the first-degree murders of three victims, the attempted first-degree murders of two victims, and leaving the scene of an accident. He was sentenced to death for each of the first-degree murders.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought review of the appellate court's affirmation of his convictions and sentences for first-degree murder, attempted first-degree murder, and leaving the scene of an accident, but the supreme court further affirmed. The death sentences were not imposed arbitrarily, the evidence supported the jury's finding that the aggravating circumstances outweighed any mitigating circumstances beyond a reasonable doubt, and the sentences were not excessive or disproportionate. Although the trial court twice applied Tenn. R. Evid. 615 in a strict manner and prevented defendant from offering his parents' mitigation testimony at sentencing, the jury was still presented with the "essence" of the excluded testimony. While the jury should have been given the opportunity to hear that proof directly from the parents, the jury's verdicts of death would have been the same even had that testimony been allowed. The death sentences were proper because the jury applied multiple aggravating circumstances as to each victim and the jury knew that it was responsible for deciding whether or not to impose the death penalty on defendant for each of the murders he committed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Mullins v. State


No. M2008-01674-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


320 S.W.3d 273; 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 867


June 2, 2010, Session Heard at Cookeville 1 


1 Oral argument was heard in this case 1 on June 2, 2010, in Cookeville, Putnam County, Tennessee, as part of this Court's S.C.A.L.E.S. (Supreme Court Advancing Legal Education for Students) project.

 
September 17, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals, Eastern Section Tennessee Claims Commission. No. T20060653. Stephanie R. Reevers, Commissioner.
Mullins v. State, 2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 227 (Tenn. Ct. App., May 15, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother brought a wrongful death action against the Tennessee Department of Children's Services (Department) for the death of her son after he was removed from her care and placed in the care of her aunt. The Tennessee Court of Appeals, Eastern Section affirmed the Tennessee Claims Commission's decision that it lacked jurisdiction for the claim pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 9-8-307(a)(1)(E) (1999 & Supp. 2009). The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The deceased child and his two brothers were removed from their mother's care because of her cocaine use and, at the mother's request and after an investigation, the Department recommended to the juvenile court that custody of the children be awarded to the mother's aunt. Less than a month later, a case worker investigated the aunt's home at the mother's request and found no basis to remove the children. Ten days later, the five-year-old boy died from extensive injuries allegedly inflicted by the aunt's 19-year-old daughter. The Claims Commission properly held that it lacked jurisdiction to hear the claim because the child was not in the care, custody, and control of the State. When the department closed a case, it no longer retained custody of a minor who was placed with a family member by juvenile court order and had no duty to supervise the home environment of such a placement. The jurisdiction of the Claims Commission was limited to the causes specifically enumerated in Tenn. Code Ann. § 9-8-307(a)(1)(E) (1999 & Supp. 2009).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was affirmed.

65 of 1427 DOCUMENTS



Gray's Disposal Co. v. Metro. Gov't of Nashville


No. M2007-00528-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


318 S.W.3d 342; 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 717


February 10, 2010, Session 
August 31, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Reversed. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals, Middle Section Chancery Court for Davidson County. Nos. 98-3317-III, 03-3890-I(III), 98-3400-II(III). Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor.
Gray's Disposal Co. v. Metro. Gov't of Nashville, 2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 304 (Tenn. Ct. App., Feb. 23, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A group of waste haulers filed an action challenging the validity of a flow control ordinance enacted by a metropolitan government. The trial court granted the government's motion for summary judgment. The appellate court reversed and remanded. The trial court limited the amount of damages to certain tipping fees. The Court of Appeals, Middle Section Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee), affirmed. The government appealed.


OVERVIEW: In reversing the trial court's initial order, the court of appeals relied on Gray's Disposal Co. v. Metro. Gov't of Nashville, Davidson Cnty, 122 S.W.3d 148 (Tenn. Ct. App. 2002). While the trial court was considering the matter on remand, the U.S. Supreme Court handed down a contrary decision in United Haulers Ass'n v. Oneida-Herkimer Sold Waste Mgmt. Auth., 550 U.S. 330 (2007). However, the trial court declined to follow the U.S. Supreme Court's intervening decision. The court of appeals relied on the law of the case doctrine and equitable principles when it affirmed. However, the Tennessee's courts were not free to disregard applicable intervening changes in federal constitutional law announced by the U.S. Supreme Court while the case was pending on remand. Accordingly, the United Haulers decision was an intervening change in controlling law for the purposes of the application of the law of the case doctrine. The lower courts' reliance on equitable principles to avoid applying the United Haulers decision was impermissible. Applying the United Haulers decision, the trial court's original order was correct.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals. It remanded the case to the trial court with directions to enter a final order consistent with its original order.

Estate of Bell v. Shelby County Health Care Corp.


No. W2008-02213-SC-S09-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


318 S.W.3d 823; 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 569


November 4, 2009, Session, Heard at Memphis 
June 24, 2010, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Estate of Bell v. Shelby County Health Care Corp., 318 S.W.3d 823, 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 719 (Tenn., Aug. 31, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed. Appeal by Permission from the Circuit Court for Shelby County. No. CT-006887-03. Rita L. Stotts, Judge.
Estate of Joyce Bell v. Shelby County Health Care Corp., 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 94 (Tenn., May 1, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action arising out of the death of a patient and injuries to her newborn son, plaintiffs, the administrator of the patient's estate and the son's guardian ad litem, appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), which granted partial summary judgment in favor of defendant, Shelby County Health Care Corporation d/b/a The Regional Medical Center (Med), pursuant to the Tennessee Governmental Tort Liability Act (GTLA).


OVERVIEW: The plaintiffs sought damages for the patient's death and injuries sustained by her newborn son, but Med filed a motion for partial summary judgment seeking the benefit of the GTLA, Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 29-20-101 to -408. At the time the injury-producing events occurred, Med was a private charitable institution; five months later, GTLA was amended to transform Med into a governmental entity. The trial court held that the GTLA applied and granted Med's summary judgment motion. The court granted the plaintiffs' application to appeal, and the plaintiffs challenged the constitutionality of legislation extending the coverage of the GTLA to Med on the ground that the legislation had been enacted after the plaintiffs had sustained their injuries. The appellate court agreed and reversed the judgment, having determined that applying the substantive amendment to the GTLA enacted after the injury-producing events occurred to the plaintiffs' damage claims violated the prohibition against retrospective laws in Tenn. Const. art. 1, § 20. Permitting Med to characterize itself as a governmental entity for the purpose of limiting its exposure to the plaintiffs' claims violated art. I, § 20.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the judgment of the circuit court and remanded the case for further proceedings.

State v. James


No. E2008-01493-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


315 S.W.3d 440; 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 570


May 5, 2010, Session 
June 24, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Hamilton County. No. 265412. Barry A. Steelman, Judge.
State v. James, 2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 400 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 5, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant, a Range I offender, was found guilty of public intoxication, theft of property over $ 1,000, and aggravated burglary and sentenced to 10 years in prison. The Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee) affirmed. Defendant was granted permission to appeal to consider the propriety of jury instructions relative to recently stolen property and the sufficiency of the circumstantial evidence to convict.


OVERVIEW: The day following a night burglary in which cash, a computer, car keys, and a car were taken from a residence, the defendant had the car keys in his possession and was driving the car on which he obtained a new title and a loan. The defendant alleged that he bought the car from a woman on the street. The supreme court held that the trial court's jury instructions properly permitted an inference that the defendant committed the burglary, There was a rational connection between the possession and the burglary. The defendant did not request special instructions or supplemental charges. The circumstantial evidence was consistent with the logical inference that the defendant was involved in the theft, either as a knowing receiver of the stolen goods or as the burglar. The trial judge properly denied an acquittal on the burglary charge and that the jury acted within its prerogative in finding the defendant guilty of burglary and rejecting his claim that he purchased the car. Finally, the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction and the trial court properly permitted jury questions of witnesses pursuant to Tenn. R. Crim. P. 24.1(c).


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the appellate court's ruling.

 

68 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Leggett v. Duke Energy Corp.


No. W2007-00788-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


308 S.W.3d 843; 2010 Tenn. LEXIS 408; 2010-1 Trade Cas. (CCH) P77,000


November 5, 2009, Session 
April 23, 2010, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Reversed. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals, Western Section Chancery Court for Fayette County. No. 13847. Martha B. Brasfield, Chancellor.
Leggett v. Duke Energy Corp., 2008 Tenn. App. LEXIS 684 (Tenn. Ct. App., Oct. 29, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff consumers filed a class action against defendant energy companies pursuant to the Tennessee Trade Practices Act (TTPA), Tenn. Code Ann. § 47-25-101 et seq. (2001). The trial court granted the companies' motion, finding that the claims were barred by field preemption and the filed rate doctrine. The consumers appealed. The Court of Appeals, Western Section Chancery Court for Fayette County (Tennessee) reversed. The companies appealed.


OVERVIEW: The consumers alleged that the companies engaged in various anticompetitive practices, including making false statements about natural gas transactions and engaging in wash trades and churning. However, the consumers' claims under the TTPA were preempted by the Natural Gas Act, 15 U.S.C.S. § 717 et seq. (2009), and subsequent federal law. Broad filed preemption was a cardinal feature of natural gas regulation. Field preemption continued to reach transactions that had been deregulated by the Natural Gas Policy Act of 1978, 15 U.S.C.S. § 3301 et seq. (2009). The field of preemption not only precluded direct price controls and ratable taking requirements, but extended to many regulations with an indirect bearing on prices. Although plausible arguments were made that in light of the Natural Gas Wellhead Decontrol Act of 1989, Pub. L. No. 101-60, 103 Stat. 157, the consumers' claims were not preempted, the state courts were bound to follow the path set out by the U.S. Supreme Court. As a result, the consumers failed to state a claim upon which relief could have been granted. Accordingly, the trial court properly dismissed their complaint.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals.

Norma Faye Pyles Lynch Family Purpose LLC v. Putnam County


No. M2008-02634-SC-R10-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


301 S.W.3d 196; 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 835


June 3, 2009, Session 
December 16, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at City of Cookeville v. Jackson, 2012 Tenn. App. LEXIS 43 (Tenn. Ct. App., Jan. 19, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 10 Extraordinary Appeal; Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed. Appeal by Permission from the Circuit Court for Putnam County. No. 08J0021. Amy Hollars, Judge.
Norma Faye Pyles Lynch Family Purpose LLC v. Putnam County, 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 249 (Tenn., May 1, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner filed an application for an extraordinary appeal, after the Court of Appeals (Tennessee) declined. The trial court denied the owner's request for an interlocutory appeal from an order granting a motion to vacate a dismissal of a condemnation action filed by appellees, a city and a county (city), consolidating the condemnation action with the owner's partition proceedings, and reserving the issue of attorney's fees.


OVERVIEW: The city filed a condemnation action but then voluntarily dismissed the complaint to allow time to obtain a certificate of public purpose and necessity as required by Tenn. Code Ann. § 13-16-207(f) (Supp. 2009). The owner then filed a motion seeking attorney's fees and costs, and filed another action seeking a partition in kind, an accounting, and damages. The city's answer contained a counterclaim to condemn the property, and the city filed a motion to set aside the voluntary dismissal. After the court granted the owner's application, the city formally abandoned its condemnation efforts and asked that the court dismiss the appeal based on mootness. The court held that the appeal should not be dismissed for mootness and that the trial court erred by failing to dismiss the city's condemnation action because it had been filed before the city obtained the certificate of public purpose and necessity under § 13-16-207(f). The city did not show that the issues had become moot as a result of the voluntary abandonment. Regardless of if the legal issues raised by the owner were moot, the case met the requirements for invoking the public interest exception to the mootness doctrine.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's orders and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

70 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Casper


No. M2006-02538-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


297 S.W.3d 676; 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 719


June 2, 2009, Session 
November 6, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Reversed. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals Circuit Court for Rutherford County. No. F-58029A. Don R. Ash, Judge.
State v. Casper, 2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 593 (Tenn. Crim. App., July 3, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a judgment from the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which reversed and dismissed defendant's convictions of 15 counts of willfully selling securities without registering with the state as a broker-dealer or agent in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 48-2-109 (1995 and Supp. 2001).


OVERVIEW: The appellate court reversed defendant's convictions after finding that the evidence was insufficient. The appellate court held that the term willfully in the criminal penalties section of the Tennessee Securities Act of 1980 required that defendant not only had to act deliberately, but also had to be aware that his conduct was prohibited by law. Upon review, the court did not agree. The court held that § 48-2-109 did not require the State of prove that defendant knew his acts were illegal in order to establish a willful violation of Tennessee securities laws. The term willfully in Tenn. Code Ann. § 48-2-123(a) (1995 and Supp. 2001) required only that defendant acted deliberately and was fully aware of his conduct. Because defendant was aware he was selling securities and knew that he was not registered as a broker-dealer or agent, defendant's convictions should have been sustained.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment and reinstated defendant's convictions and sentences.

Goff v. Elmo Greer & Sons Constr. Co.


No. M2006-02660-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


297 S.W.3d 175; 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 701; 40 ELR 20254; 70 ERC (BNA) 2137


June 2, 2009, Session 
November 3, 2009, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Elmo Greer & Sons Constr. v. Goff, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 2621 (U.S., Mar. 22, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Reversed; Judgment of the Trial Court Reinstated as Modified. Appeal by permission from the Court of Appeals, Middle Section, Circuit Court for White County. No. CC-320. John A. Turnbull, Judge.
Goff v. Elmo Greer & Sons Constr. Co., 2008 Tenn. App. LEXIS 296 (Tenn. Ct. App., May 16, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Reversed; Judgment of the Trial Court Reinstated as Modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners sued defendant construction company alleging breach of contract, nuisance and other claims with regard to the unlawful disposal of hazardous waste on their property. The Court of Appeals, Middle Section, Circuit Court for White County (Tenn.) affirmed the trial court's award of liability but reversed the award of punitive damages. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owners agreed to let the company use their property to place equipment and construction materials on their land in exchange for compensation. The company buried old tires, spilled oil and caused blasting damage to their house and vehicles. At trial, the parties stipulated that the company was liable for breach of contract in the amount of $ 5,355.50. A jury then determined that the company was strictly liable for harm caused by its blasting activities in the amount of $ 9,510, and that burying debris on the property constituted a nuisance for which the company was liable for $ 3,305. The jury also returned an award of $ 2 million in punitive damages which the trial court modified to $ 1 million. The appellate court reversed the punitive damages award on the grounds that the trial court improperly considered Tennessee's environmental laws in approving the award. The supreme court found that the evidence supported the jury's award of punitive damages and that the trial court properly considered Tennessee's environmental statutes in approving that award. However, the award was excessive and violated the company's due process rights. As such, the court would modify the award.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the court of appeals was reversed; Judgment of the trial court was reinstated as modified. The amount of punitive damages was modified to an award of $ 500,000.

State v. Turner


No. W2007-01590-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


297 S.W.3d 155; 2009 Tenn. LEXIS 678


April 8, 2009, Session 
October 15, 2009, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Reversed; Remanded. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals, Circuit Court for Obion County. No. C07-192. William B. Acree, Jr., Judge.
State v. Turner, 2008 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 321 (Tenn. Crim. App., Apr. 29, 2008)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Reversed; Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the Court of Criminal Appeals, Circuit Court for Obion County (Tennessee) upheld the trial court's decision to grant defendant's motion to suppress, the instant court granted the State permission to appeal to determine whether the police violated the constitutional rights of defendant, a parolee, when they searched her residence without a warrant but pursuant to a condition of her parole.


OVERVIEW: The trial court erred in granting the motion to suppress and the Court of Criminal Appeals erred in affirming the trial court. The warrantless search of defendant's residence, made pursuant to a written condition of her parole, was reasonable under the U.S. Const. amend. IV and Tenn. Const. art. I, § 7, even if made without any reasonable, individualized, or particularized suspicion. Under the totality of the circumstances, the police officer's decision to search defendant's residence was not unreasonable. There was no proof that the officer acted for any reason other than the furtherance of legitimate law enforcement concerns. Defendant had been convicted of drug offenses in two states. The officer had information from an informant that she was involved in selling crack cocaine. He verified defendant's parole status and the warrantless search condition before he searched her residence. Neither the search of defendant's vehicle nor that of her residence was unreasonably lengthy. That the total time of defendant's detention might have been at most two hours and included a short trip by defendant in her own vehicle did not so prolong the detention as to make the search unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of criminal appeals was reversed, and the matter was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Colonial Pipeline Co. v. Morgan


No. M2006-00591-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


263 S.W.3d 827; 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 589


June 4, 2008, Session 
September 9, 2008, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals. Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 05-748-IV. Richard H. Dinkins, Chancellor.
Colonial Pipeline Co. v. Morgan, 2007 Tenn. App. LEXIS 408 (Tenn. Ct. App., July 2, 2007)
ANR Pipeline Co. v. TN Bd. of Equalization, 2002 Tenn. App. LEXIS 897 (Tenn. Ct. App., Dec. 19, 2002)
Colonial Pipeline Co. v. Morgan, 474 F.3d 211, 2007 U.S. App. LEXIS 358 (6th Cir. Tenn., 2007)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Davidson County, Tennessee, dismissed appellee pipeline company's suit for declaratory judgment, challenging the constitutionality of specified portions of the state tax code and seeking an injunction as to the enforcement of those provisions. The Tennessee Court of Appeals reversed and remanded. Appellant State petitioned for review.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the court of appeals erred by holding that the chancery court had jurisdiction to hear the constitutional challenge without the company first submitting the claim to the Board of Equalization and holding that declaratory judgment was an available remedy against state officers in tax cases. The supreme court found that Tenn. Code Ann. § 67-5-1327 (2006) did not preclude the company's suit for declaratory judgment and was not a barrier to a constitutional challenge to the facial validity of the statute. Section 4-5-225 did not preclude the chancery court from considering a constitutional challenge to the facial validity of a statute even when the agency had not considered a declaratory order. The chancery court improperly dismissed the complaint for failure to exhaust administrative remedies. The company's argument of inherent bias was without merit. The chancery court could issue declaratory and injunctive relief against the State officers in their individual capacity, so long as the judgment was tailored to prevent the implementation of unconstitutional legislation and did not reach the state, its treasury, funds, or property, Tenn. Code Ann. § 20-13-102.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was affirmed and the case was remanded to the chancery court for further proceedings.


 

81 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Allen


No. W2006-01080-SC-R11-CD, No. W2005-02805-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


259 S.W.3d 671; 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 419


April 2, 2008, Session 
June 24, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at Allen v. State, 2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 209 (Tenn. Crim. App., Mar. 22, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11; Judgments of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Appeal by permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Shelby County. Nos. 00-10541-47; 00-10550-56. John P. Colton, Jr., Judge. Appeal by permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 03-08391. W. Mark Ward, Judge.
State v. Allen, 2007 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 506 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 25, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two separate cases, defendants were convicted of multiple offenses and were ultimately given consecutive sentences. The Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) affirmed, and defendants appealed, arguing that the trial court's imposition of consecutive sentences violated the Sixth Amendment as interpreted by the Supreme Court in Apprendi and its progeny.


OVERVIEW: Prior to ordering consecutive sentences, the trial court in each of the cases at hand found the defendant to be a "dangerous offender" for purposes of Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-115(b)(4). Under the Apprendi rule, other than the fact of a prior conviction, any fact that increased the penalty for a crime beyond the statutory maximum had to be submitted to a jury and proved beyond a reasonable doubt. In rejecting defendants' challenge to their sentences on the basis of the Apprendi rule, the supreme court reasoned that: (1) the principles underlying Apprendi did not apply to consecutive sentences because a judge's decision on how two separate sentences for two distinct crimes should be served was different from the jury's determination of whether the elements of a crime, necessary for a particular sentence, were committed; and (2) the findings supporting defendants' "dangerous offender" status were the types of factors that assisted a judge in determining the manner in which a defendant should serve sentences for multiple offenses, but were not the functional equivalents of elements a jury would consider in determining whether a defendant committed a greater or lesser crime.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the intermediate appellate court were affirmed.

State v. Cannon


No. E2005-01237-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


254 S.W.3d 287; 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 278


January 8, 2008, Session 
April 29, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at State v. Cannon, 2012 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 982 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 5, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals is Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part and Remanded. Appeal by permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Hamilton County. No. 243913. Rebecca J. Stern, Judge.
State v. Cannon, 2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 994 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 27, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals is Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of aggravated rape. The Court of Criminal Appeals of Tennessee affirmed his conviction but remanded the case for re-sentencing. The state supreme court granted defendant permission to appeal.


OVERVIEW: The eighty-two year old victim reported that an unknown assailant raped her in her home. The victim did not testify at trial. Defendant was convicted of aggravated rape. On appeal, he challenged the admission of evidence and the violation of his confrontation rights. The Supreme Court of Tennessee concluded that the State failed to establish a proper chain of custody for the admission into evidence of the victim's pantyhose. The error was not harmless, because the only tangible evidence linking defendant to the victim was the DNA analysis derived from the semen found on the pantyhose. The victim's statements describing the assault to the police officers and her statements to the sexual assault nurse examiner were testimonial and admitted in violation of defendant's right of confrontation. The collection of defendant's blood sample for DNA testing while he was incarcerated for an unrelated offense did not violate his constitutional rights. The trial court properly denied defendant's motion for recusal, based on the mere existence of a friendship between the judge and the assistant district attorney.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for aggravated rape was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new trial.

State v. Rimmer


No. W2004-02240-SC-DDT-DD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


250 S.W.3d 12; 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 108


November 14, 2007, Session 
February 20, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 17, 2008.

As Corrected November 12, 2008.
Rehearing denied by State v. Rimmer, 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 203 (Tenn., Mar. 26, 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Rimmer v. Tennessee, 555 U.S. 852, 129 S. Ct. 111, 172 L. Ed. 2d 88, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 6756 (2008)
Application denied by, Stay denied by Rimmer v. State, 2011 Tenn. LEXIS 1066 (Tenn., Nov. 8, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(a)(1); Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Automatic Appeal from the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 98-01033-34. W. Fred Axley, Circuit Judge.
State v. Rimmer, 2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 986 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 15, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of theft, aggravated robbery, and premeditated murder and was sentenced to death. The Tennessee Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court found that the death sentence was not disproportionate and not arbitrary. Defendant, an estranged boyfriend, murdered an ex-girlfriend, whose testimony had sent him to prison for rape. While he was in prison, he had confided to other inmates his intentions to harm the victim. The threats defendant had made suggested that the murder was a premeditated act of vengeance. That the murder took place shortly after his release from prison buttressed that inference. The proof established that on the night of the murder, defendant sought out the victim at her place of employment, murdered her, and disposed of her body. While the means of her death was not entirely clear, the bloody crime scene indicated that there was a violent struggle. The body was never recovered. Defendant, having a prior criminal record for violent crimes, was convicted on overwhelmingly persuasive circumstantial evidence. Based on the testimony of two prison inmates, he had planned the murder as an act of revenge. He approached the victim at a time when she was most vulnerable - alone and working after midnight at a hotel.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

R.D.S. v. State


No. M2005-00213-SC-R11-JV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


245 S.W.3d 356; 2008 Tenn. LEXIS 28


October 3, 2007, Session 
February 6, 2008, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected February 7, 2008.
On remand at, Remanded by State v. R.D.S., 2009 Tenn. App. LEXIS 440 (Tenn. Ct. App., July 16, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part and Remanded. Appeal by permission from the Court of Appeals, Middle Section Circuit Court for Williamson County. No. II-CR04274. R.E. Lee Davies, Judge.
State v. R.D.S., 2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 733 (Tenn. Ct. App., Nov. 17, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, was adjudicated delinquent for the acts of simple possession or casual exchange of marijuana and possession of drug paraphernalia after his motion to suppress evidence was denied. The Tennessee Court of Appeals, Middle Section Circuit Court for Williamson County affirmed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress his statements because he was in custody. The supreme court disagreed. The deputy testified that when she and the vice-principal found defendant prior to searching his truck, she told him about another student and that they were "going out to the vehicle to search the vehicle because of the other student's apparently intoxicated condition." She said that she did not "tell him" to accompany them, but rather "advised him" of their discovery and "requested that he go with us since it was his vehicle." The court of appeals looked at the totality of the circumstances, including the language and substance of the request, the fact that the questioning took place in the parking lot and while walking between the school and the parking lot, and that defendant was not confined to the principal's office for questioning. However, with respect to the evidence seized, the parties failed to present sufficient evidence for the trial court to conclude whether the deputy's duties allowed her to conduct a search based upon reasonable suspicion or whether the search should have been based upon probable cause.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the trial court so the parties could present more evidence on the issue of whether the deputy's duties allowed her to conduct a search based upon reasonable suspicion or whether the search should be based upon probable cause. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

State v. Gomez


No. M2002-01209-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


239 S.W.3d 733; 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 884


June 7, 2007, Session 
October 9, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at State v. Gomez, 2009 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 819 (Tenn. Crim. App., Sept. 29, 2009)
Appeal after remand at State v. Londono, 2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 125 (Tenn. Crim. App., Feb. 24, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11; Judgments of the Trial Court Affirmed in Part, Vacated and Remanded in Part. On remand from the United States Supreme Court Davidson County Criminal Court. No. 2001-A-280. Cheryl Blackburn, Judge.
Gomez v. Tennessee, 549 U.S. 1190, 127 S. Ct. 1209, 167 L. Ed. 2d 36, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 1852 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Trial Court Affirmed in Part, Vacated and Remanded in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged a decision from the Davidson County Criminal Court (Tennessee), which convicted them of conspiracy to commit aggravated robbery, facilitation of felony murder, facilitation of especially aggravated robbery, and facilitation of aggravated robbery and imposed the maximum sentence. After the decision was affirmed, the case was heard by the United States Supreme Court, which remanded the case for reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: After defendants were convicted of various crimes, the maximum sentences were imposed by the trial court. It relied on several aggravating factors under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-114(1), (2), (9) (Supp. 2001). The convictions and sentences were affirmed. However, the United States Supreme Court remanded the case for reconsideration. In vacating the sentences, the Tennessee Supreme Court determined that the trial court was not allowed to impose the maximum sentence without finding aggravating factors. However, the judicial imposition of enhancement factors § 40-35-114(2) and (9) deprived defendants of their Sixth Amendment right to have a jury determine whether those enhancement factors applied. Defense counsel had not waived the right to assert this error; there was no basis for relief under Apprendi until after Blakely was decided. Because the trial court's error adversely affected defendants' unwaived rights to a jury trial, and because the record on appeal did allow a determination of the proper sentences to be imposed, substantial justice required the Tennessee Supreme Court to vacate the sentences. Finally, all of the elements of plain error were established.


OUTCOME: The sentences were vacated, and the case was remanded for resentencing. In all other respects, the decision was affirmed.

State v. Berrios


No. W2005-01179-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


235 S.W.3d 99; 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 745


April 3, 2007, Session 
August 17, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Appeal by permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 04-03042. Paula Skahan, Judge.
State v. Berrios, 2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 193 (Tenn. Crim. App., Mar. 3, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A trial court granted defendant's motion to suppress cocaine seized during a traffic stop, and the Court of Criminal Appeals of Tennessee affirmed. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: A police officer stopped defendant's vehicle for speeding, frisked him and placed him in the back of his patrol car, and after defendant consented, searched his vehicle and discovered 300 grams of cocaine hidden in the fender. On appeal of the trial court's decision granting defendant's motion to suppress, the court held that even though the initial stop of defendant's vehicle was constitutionally permissible, as he was speeding, the officer's frisking defendant and placing him in the patrol car was not, and therefore the motion was properly granted. The officer had no suspicion that defendant was armed or dangerous, and he did not check the validity of defendant's driver's license or vehicle registration before frisking him or placing him in the patrol car. The record established that the officer placed defendant in the patrol car primarily to determine whether he became more nervous, and the officer's record showed that he conducted "frisks and sits" in other instances regardless of the weather or the time of day. Defendant's consent to the search of his vehicle was not sufficiently attenuated from the violation of his constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment granting defendant's motion to suppress was affirmed.

Lanier v. Rains


No. M2005-00128-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


229 S.W.3d 656; 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 583


February 2, 2007, Session 
June 28, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part and Remanded. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals, Eastern Section Chancery Court for Fentress County, Probate Division. No. P-04-30. Billy Joe White, Chancellor.
Lanier v. Rains, 2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 61 (Tenn. Ct. App., Jan. 11, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Tennessee Court of Appeals affirmed the judgment of the Chancery Court for Fentress County, Tennessee, in sustaining a motion to dismiss filed on behalf of defendants, the decedent's estate and his wife and son as co-executors, on petitioner heir's legitimation after the decedent's death so as to share in his estate as a pretermitted heir. The heir appealed.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court determined that, pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 32-3-103 (2001), the heir was not "born" subsequent to the execution of the will. The legislature expressed no intent to attach such a liberal construction to the word "born." The heir had been disinherited by implication. If the testator intended to omit the child from the will, the pretermitted heir statute was inapplicable, regardless of whether the child was legitimate, born out of wedlock, or adopted. Because the decedent, if fully aware of his relationship to the heir, made no effort to adopt or formally to legitimate her after the execution of his will, disinheritance by implication was established. The heir could not prevail on constitutional grounds as the expansive definition of "born" that existed for an adopted child who sought to qualify as a pretermitted heir did not constitute a denial of equal protection. The legitimation issue had to be remanded to the trial court to permit the heir to present her claim pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 31-2-105, the parent-child relationship statute, to demonstrate a relationship to the decedent for purposes of establishing intestate succession rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was affirmed where the heir did not qualify as a pretermitted heir; the claim for legitimation was remanded to the chancery court.

State v. Flood


No. E2005-00878-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


219 S.W.3d 307; 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 274


January 3, 2007, Session  
March 15, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 15, 2007
Post-conviction relief denied at Flood v. State, 2010 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 251 (Tenn. Crim. App., Mar. 24, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 11; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals is Reversed. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 69716. Ray L. Jenkins, Judge.
State v. Flood, 2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 150 (Tenn. Crim. App., Feb. 2, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals is Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of four counts of rape of a child. The Tennessee Court of Criminal Appeals reversed the convictions and remanded the case for a new trial. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by excluding evidence of two statements made by the victim to her father, and that the exclusion violated his right to present a defense. The supreme court disagreed. The first statement was that defendant had made the victim touch his penis. The second was the victim asking her father if defendant would still have to go jail if someone else were caught. The trial court excluded the testimony from the victim's father on two grounds: (1) that the testimony was inadmissible hearsay; and (2) that the testimony was inadmissible extrinsic evidence of a prior inconsistent statement. The statements had little probative value to implicate another in the crime or to rebut the victim's testimony that oral penetration occurred. In fact, it could be argued that the excluded statements tended to support the prosecution as much they tended to support the defense. Although the statements appeared reliable, they had little probative value to implicate another in the crime or rebut the victim's testimony. The trial court's exclusion of the statements did not rise to the level of a constitutional violation because they were not critical to the defense.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of criminal appeals was reversed.

Edwards v. Allen


No. M2004-01944-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


216 S.W.3d 278; 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 144


October 5, 2006, Session  
March 2, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed; Case Remanded. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals, Middle Section Chancery Court for Rutherford County. No. 036806. Robert E. Corlew, III, Chancellor.
Edwards v. Allen, 2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 739 (Tenn. Ct. App., Nov. 28, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff neighbors sued defendants, shooting range owners, leaseholders, a mayor, and a county, alleging that a property reclassification violated a county zoning resolution and Tenn. Code Ann. § 13-7-105 (1992). A chancery court granted defendants' motion to dismiss for untimeliness. The Court of Appeals (Tennessee) reversed the chancery court ruling and found that the county resolution was void ab initio. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: In 1992, residential property was reclassified to allow a shooting range. Although the notice and hearing involved a 10-acre parcel, the adopted resolution reclassified 90 acres. The neighbors filed suit in 2003 after the leaseholders began expanding. The supreme court determined that the resolution qualified as a zoning amendment, rather than a special exception or conditional use permit, and the procedural requirements of Tenn. Code Ann. § 13-7-105 applied because (1) the request was presented to a planning commission rather than a board of zoning appeals, and (2) the request to allow a for-profit shooting range on property zoned as residential for single family dwellings substantially affected the use of the land. The ordinance was void ab initio and the statute of limitations was no defense because (1) the county legislative body had no jurisdiction to act on the proposed zoning amendment since the alteration was so substantial that there should have been a resubmission of the proposed amendment to the planning commission, and (2) the record did not establish the requisite public or private reliance for an exception to the application of the void ab initio doctrine.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court and remanded the case to the chancery court.
