State v. Riels


No. W2004-02832-SC-DDT-DD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


216 S.W.3d 737; 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 142


November 15, 2006, Session  
March 1, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(a)(1); Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Reversed and Remanded. Automatic Appeal from the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 03-06530. Chris Craft, Judge.
State v. Riels, 2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 273 (Tenn. Crim. App., Mar. 31, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to, inter alia, two counts of premeditated murder and two counts of felony murder and was sentenced to death. The Tennessee Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed the sentences. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in allowing the State to cross-examine him regarding the circumstances of the crimes. The supreme court agreed. Defendant's statements were simply his attempt at expressing remorse to the victims' families and friends about the crimes that he had already admitted committing. It was troubling that the trial court called the parties to the bench and sua sponte announced that defendant opened the door for the cross-examination. At that time, the State had not yet raised the issue and might never have raised the issue. By finding that defendant's statements of remorse opened the door to full cross-examination on the circumstances of the crimes, the trial court violated defendant's right to avoid self-incrimination. While defendant had already admitted his culpability for the crimes charged by pleading guilty, he still had the constitutional right not to be a witness against himself. While the evidence already before the jury gave them a fairly clear picture of what happened during the attack, hearing such details from third parties did not have nearly the same impact as hearing detailed, graphic descriptions from defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of criminal appeals was reversed and the case was remanded for a new capital sentencing hearing.

Bredesen v. Tenn. Judicial Selection Comm'n


No. M2006-02722-SC-RDM-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


214 S.W.3d 419; 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 121


February 1, 2007, Session  
February 21, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
As Corrected February 22, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  Tenn. Code Ann. § 16-3-201(d); Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed, As Modified. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 06-2275-III. Ellen H. Lyle, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed, As Modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the Governor of Tennessee, filed a complaint in the Chancery Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) against defendant, the Tennessee Judicial Selection Commission, alleging, inter alia, that a second panel submitted by the Commission was not valid under Tenn. Code Ann. § 17-4-112(a) as it contained the name of a rejected nominee from the first panel. The court found for the governor, the Commission and intervenors, two judges, appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Commission argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in its determination of the appropriate remedy by ordering the Commission to certify and submit to the governor a second panel of nominees, which panel could not include the names of prior nominees. The supreme court agreed. The trial court's remedy unduly restricted the Commission's authority under the Tennessee Plan because the Tennessee Plan left the basic operating procedures to Commission's discretion. Because an ineligible nominee was included on the second panel certified to the Governor, the statutory requirement that the Commission certify "the names of three persons," Tenn. Code Ann. § 17-4-109(e), was never satisfied; under those circumstances, the panel was void ab initio, and the Commission must reinstitute the selection process for all three nominees to be included on the second panel. Even if the panel was not void ab initio, under Tenn. Code Ann. § 17-4-109(e), in order to make an informed judgment as to which applicants were the three persons "best qualified and available," the Commission necessarily must compare each applicant with all of the other applicants who sought to fill the judicial vacancy.


OUTCOME: The Commission was required to re-institute the selection process for all three of the nominees to be certified to the governor as the second panel. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

State v. Pickett


No. M2004-00732-SC-R11-CD, No. M2004-01811-SC-R11-CO


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


211 S.W.3d 696; 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 10


October 4, 2006, Session  
January 22, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Harwood v. Tennessee, 128 S. Ct. 436, 169 L. Ed. 2d 305, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 11604 (U.S., Oct. 15, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgments of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Appeal by permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2002-C-1439, No. 2003-B-843. Steve Dozier, Judge.
State v. Harwood, 2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 988 (Tenn. Crim. App., Sept. 7, 2005)
State v. Pickett, 2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1076 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 3, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: From separate trials, defendant one was found guilty of sexual exploitation of a minor, while defendant two was indicted on the same charge. Both defendants challenged the constitutionality of former Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-1003 (2003). The Tennessee Court of Criminal appeals held that the statute was not unconstitutional, but dismissed 10 of defendant one's 11 convictions as multiplicitous. Both defendant's sought review.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendants again asserted that the statute was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. The State contended the appellate court erred by ruling that 10 of defendant one's 11 convictions were multiplicitous. The supreme court found that former Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-17-1003(b) (2003), which permitted the trier of fact to infer that the image was of a minor, did not alter the requirement that the image be of "a minor." Thus, this subsection, a permissive inference, was not unconstitutionally overbroad. Further, the statute did not impermissibly shift the burden to defendants to prove that the image did not depict a minor. And because the possession contemplated by the statute had to be "knowing," a person who inadvertently stumbled upon child pornography would not be guilty of a crime under the terms of the statute. Thus, the statute was not unconstitutionally vague. Finally, the supreme court disagreed with the State's contention and agreed with the appellate court's finding that because the State presented no evidence concerning which pictures came from which website or when defendant one accessed each picture, the evidence established only one crime.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgments were affirmed.

Jordan v. Knox County


No. E2006-01377-SC-RDM-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


213 S.W.3d 751; 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 26


September 6, 2006, Session  
January 12, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Seider v. Hutchison, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 6730 (E.D. Tenn., Jan. 30, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. Code Ann. § 16-3-201(d); Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court for Knox County. No. 166799-1 John. F. Weaver, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a county, its election commission, and the state administrator of elections, challenged a decision from the Knox County Chancery Court, which entered judgment in favor of plaintiff county commissioners by determining that a county charter and an amendment to such pertaining to term limitations were invalid.


OVERVIEW: The commissioners contended that the county did not properly adopt an alternative form of government. According to them, the term-limit provision amending the charter did not affect their ability to run for office. The chancery court found that the charter and the amendment were invalid, and this appeal followed. In partially reversing, the supreme court held that the charter was not valid because it did not provide for the constitutional county offices or otherwise assign their duties under Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 5-1-203(b), 5-1-202. Therefore, the charter established a de facto form of government. Under this equitable doctrine, the county government had a valid existence. Moreover, its elected officials, as de facto officers, exercised the traditional duties of their offices. As such, the term limits amendment under Knox County, Tenn., County Charter art. VIII, § 8.17, enacted under the de facto charter, was upheld as a component of the governmental unit. The amendment applied to all elected officials, except for those protected by statute or the state constitution. Under Tenn. Const. art. VII, § 1, the county commissioners were subject to term limitations.


OUTCOME: The portion of the decision invalidating the charter was affirmed, but the invalidation of the terms limit amendment was reversed.

State v. Reid


No. M2003-00539-SC-DDT-DD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


213 S.W.3d 792; 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 1203


October 6, 2006, Session  
December 27, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Reid, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 17 (Tenn., Jan. 17, 2007)
Motion granted by Reid v. Tennessee, 127 S. Ct. 2966, 168 L. Ed. 2d 260, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 7519 (U.S., 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Reid v. Tenn., 2007 U.S. LEXIS 11530 (U.S., Oct. 15, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(a)(1); Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Automatic Appeal from the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 97-C-1836. Cheryl Blackburn, Judge.
State v. Reid, 2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 556 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 3, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of three counts of premeditated murder, three counts of felony murder, one count of attempted murder, and one count of especially aggravated robbery. Each of the felony murder convictions was merged with the corresponding premeditated murder convictions and defendant was sentenced to death. The Tennessee Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by finding that he was competent to stand trial. The supreme court disagreed. The trial court determined that defendant was able to consult with his counsel and otherwise assist in the preparation of his defense. The evidence in the record did not preponderate against the trial court's findings. The trial court heard and specifically accredited the testimony of the independent expert witnesses. In addition, the trial court found that defendant himself had expressed an understanding of the proceedings. Although defendant had been diagnosed by his experts with anosognosia, the trial court was free to assess their credibility and reject their testimony. One of defendant's experts admitted that defendant had a previous history of malingering, he had rationally discussed many facets of his case with his attorneys, and he understood the roles of the prosecutor, the judge, and the defense attorneys. Moreover, the trial court applied the correct legal standard: whether defendant had the capacity to understand the nature and object of the proceedings against him, to consult with counsel, and to assist in preparing his defense.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

McCarver v. Ins. Co. of Pa.


No. M2005-02288-SC-R3-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


208 S.W.3d 380; 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 1133


October 5, 2006, Session  
December 13, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-225(e) (2005); Judgment of the General Sessions Court is Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the General Sessions Court of Warren County. Nos. 8958 & 9045. Larry G. Ross, Judge.
McCarver v. Ins. Co. of Pa., 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 335 (Tenn., May 4, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the General Sessions Court is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, an employer and its insurer, appealed a decision of the General Sessions Court of Warren County (Tennessee), which denied defendants' motion challenging its subject matter jurisdiction and ultimately found plaintiff claimant to be 88.2% disabled because of a workers' compensation injury pursuant to the Workers' Compensation Law, Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-101 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The court granted review to determine whether Tenn. Code Ann. § 16-15-5004(c), granting jurisdiction over workers' compensation cases to the General Sessions Court for Warren County, violated Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 8. On review, the court upheld the trial court's jurisdiction and the disability award. Even though the Workers' Compensation law, Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-101 et seq., applied uniformly throughout the state and Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-225(a)(1) conferred jurisdiction of such claims to circuit, criminal, and chancery courts, Tenn. Code Ann. § 16-15-5004(c) did not violate Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 98 because there was a rational basis for the classification. Under Tenn. Code Ann. § 16-2-506(31)(A), a single judge sat as the chancellor, circuit court judge, and criminal court judge for two counties, and granting the general sessions court jurisdiction over workers' compensation cases more reasonably allocated the caseload among the available judges. The court also found that the evidence did not preponderate against the trial court's findings of disability under Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-241 in that the findings were within the range found by vocational experts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Lynch v. City of Jellico


No. E2006-00208-SC-R3-CV, No. E2006-00207-SC-R3-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


205 S.W.3d 384; 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 759


June 8, 2006, Session  
August 30, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition denied by Lynch v. City of Jellico, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 943 (Tenn., Oct. 10, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Lynch v. Jellico, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 3049 (U.S., Mar. 19, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-225(e); Judgments of the Trial Court Reversed; Remanded. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court Campbell County, Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court Claiborne County. No. 05-100, No. 150-63 Billy Joe White, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Trial Court Reversed; Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employers appealed a decision of the Chancery Court Campbell County (Tennessee), which held that the mandatory benefit review conference in Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 50-6-203(a), 50-6-225(a)(1), and 50-6-239(b) violated due process under the Tennessee and U.S. Constitutions; the Separation of Powers doctrine of Tenn. Const. art. II, §§ 1 and 2; and Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-225.


OVERVIEW: The claimants filed separate actions challenging the constitutionality of provisions of the Workers' Compensation Reform Act of 2004. The trial judge concluded that the benefit review conference deprived injured workers of their rights to a trial by judge or an individual otherwise learned in the law. The court reversed and held that the claimants failed to establish that the conference was inconsistent with basic notions of fairness or fair process. Because injured workers were free to file suit and have their rights judicially determined upon exhausting the benefit review process, they were not deprived of their right to be heard by a judge. Nor did the benefit review conference violate substantive due process. The claimants did not show the deprivation of any particular constitutional right, much less a fundamental one. Further, the court was not persuaded that requiring parties to participate in a benefit review conference prior to seeking redress in the courts was an "arbitrary, or conscience shocking" exercise of the legislature's authority to craft the workers' compensation system.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

 

97 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


In re T.K.Y.


No. M2004-01634-SC-R11-JV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


205 S.W.3d 343; 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 757


March 21, 2006, Session  
August 28, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by In re T.K.Y., 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 891 (Tenn., Sept. 19, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Reversed; Case Remanded to Trial Court. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals Juvenile Court for Coffee County. No. 368-99J. Timothy R. Brock, Judge.
In re TKY, 2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 415 (Tenn. Ct. App., July 14, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Reversed; Case Remanded to Trial Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A trial court determined that appellant biological father was the legal father of a child. On appeal, the Court of Appeals Juvenile Court for Coffee County (Tennessee) reversed, and held that the biological mother's husband was the child's legal father under Tenn. Code Ann. § 36-2-304(a). The biological father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother engaged in an extramarital affair with the biological father and became pregnant. The mother and her husband remained married after she revealed her affair and the husband held the child out to the world as his child despite DNA tests to the contrary. The biological father subsequently petitioned to establish his parentage, custody, visitation, and child support; the mother and her husband petitioned to terminate the biological father's parental rights. The appellate court held that the husband was the child's legal father based on the best interests of the child. On appeal, the court reversed. Pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 36-2-302, 24-7-112, the biological father was the legal father of the child, absent the termination of his rights. A best-interests analysis was relevant if an only if termination was appropriate. The court affirmed the trial court's determination that the evidence did not support the arguments of the mother and her husband that the biological father willfully failed to visit or support the child. The evidence showed that the mother actively concealed the child's parentage and that the mother declined the biological father's offer of support.


OUTCOME: The judgment reversing the trial court's decision that the father was the child's legal father was reversed, and the child support order was modified. The case was remanded to the juvenile court for a calculation of child support and retroactive child support consistent with the opinion.

State v. Scarborough


Nos. E2004-01332-SC-R11-CD, Nos. W2004-01475-SC-R11-CD, W2003-02966-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


201 S.W.3d 607; 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 758


February 1, 2006, Session  
August 28, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. 9; Tenn. R. App. 11; Judgments of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Appeal by permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 75589. Mary Beth Leibowitz, Judge. Appeal by permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals Circuit Court for Madison County. Nos. 02-359, 02-360. Roy B. Morgan, Jr., Judge.
State v. Scarborough, 2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 544 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 2, 2005)
State v. Transou, 2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 664 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 30, 2005)
State v. Transou, 2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 463 (Tenn. Crim. App., May 13, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The first defendant appealed a judgment of the Courts of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Knox County (Tennessee) denying his motion to suppress deoxyribonucleic acid (DNA) evidence from his rape case. The second defendant appealed a judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Circuit Court for Madison County (Tennessee) convicting him of two counts of rape, one count of sexual battery, and one count of aggravated burglary.


OVERVIEW: While defendants were incarcerated for other crimes, their blood was taken and DNA analysis identified them as the perpetrators of the instant crimes. On appeal, defendants argued that the extraction of blood from convicted and incarcerated felons for DNA analysis under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-321 (2003) violated the Fourth Amendment and Tenn. Const. art. I, § 7. The court held that § 40-35-321 was constitutional as applied to the first defendant, and therefore the trial court did not err by denying his motion to suppress, because the blood draw and its subsequent analysis were reasonable under all of the circumstances, which included the facts that: (1) the gravity of the public concern served by the searches was significant, given that DNA more accurately identified those who committed and were convicted of felonies; (2) § 40-35-321 clearly and unambiguously specified who was subject to the searches; (3) no measure of individualized suspicion was necessary because the searches were not aimed at recovering incriminating evidence of contemporaneous criminal conduct; and (4) the convicted felons subject to search had a significantly reduced expectation of privacy.


OUTCOME: The judgments denying the first defendant's motion to suppress and convicting the second defendant were affirmed.

ACLU v. Darnell


No. M2006-00460-SC-RDM-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


195 S.W.3d 612; 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 610


June 7, 2006, Session  
July 14, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. Code Ann. § 16-3-201; Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Chancery Court of Davidson County. No. 05-1010-IV. Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, organizations, citizens, and three members of the Tennessee House of Representatives, filed a complaint in the Davidson County Chancery Court, Tennessee, against defendants, state officials, seeking to enjoin the Secretary of State from including the Marriage Amendment to Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 3, on the November 7, 2006, ballot. The chancellor denied the request. Plaintiffs sought review.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs argued that Tenn. Const. art. XI, § 3 provided a mandatory sequential process that could only be satisfied by literal compliance, and that the failure to publish the Marriage Amendment six months prior to the 2004 election constituted a deviation from the constitutional mandates and precluded it from appearing on the November 7, 2006 ballot. The supreme court found that plaintiffs failed to establish a distinct, concrete injury in fact resulting from the alleged untimely publication of the Marriage Amendment. Plaintiffs failed to establish that the alleged untimely publication impaired their right to vote in the 2004 election or precluded them from supporting candidates in the 2004 election who opposed the Marriage Amendment. Plaintiffs' sexual orientation and interest in same gender marriage were not relevant to their claim that the Marriage Amendment was not published in accordance with art. XI, § 3. The legislator plaintiffs failed to establish that the effectiveness of their vote or any of their other legislative powers was impeded by the alleged untimely publication. The organizational plaintiffs lacked standing to maintain the lawsuit.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

100 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Reid v. State


No. M2005-00260-SC-S09-PC


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


197 S.W.3d 694; 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 555


February 2, 2006, Session  
June 26, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Reid v. State, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 643 (Tenn., July 20, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 9(c); Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed as Modified; Remanded to the Trial Court. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals. Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 97-C-1834. Cheryl Blackburn, Judge.
Holton v. State, 201 S.W.3d 626, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 331 (Tenn., May 4, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Trial Court Affirmed as Modified; Remanded to the Trial Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought post-conviction relief under the Post-Conviction Procedure Act, Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-101 et seq., from his murder convictions and death sentences. He appealed an order of the Criminal Court for Davidson County (Tennessee) setting forth a procedure for determining competency to proceed at the post-conviction level and adopting the Nix standard for mental incompetence.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of two counts of first-degree murder and was sentenced to death. He sought post-conviction relief, and his counsel claimed that he was incompetent. The trial court's order set forth a procedure for determining the inmate's competency and granted him an interlocutory appeal under Tenn. R. App. P. 9. On appeal, the court held that the civil standard for mental incompetence adopted in State v. Nix, applied to a competency determination during post-conviction proceedings. To trigger a hearing on competency, the inmate had to make a prima facie showing of incompetence by submission of affidavits, depositions, medical reports, or other credible evidence. The inmate bore the burden of proving that he was incompetent by clear and convincing evidence. A finding of incompetence required neither a stay of the post-conviction proceedings nor abeyance of individual issues; the trial court should appoint, if necessary, a "next friend" or guardian ad litem to pursue the action on behalf of the inmate.


OUTCOME: The order was modified such that rather than a bifurcated procedure that would hold factual claims that required a petitioner's input in abeyance pending his return to competency, a next friend or guardian ad litem would be appointed to pursue the action on the petitioner's behalf. As modified, the order was affirmed.

State v. Stephenson


No. E2003-01091-SC-DDT-DD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


195 S.W.3d 574; 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 454


January 4, 2006, Argued  
June 2, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Stephenson v. Bell, 2012 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 420 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 20, 2012)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Stephenson v. State, 2013 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1114 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 19, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(a)(1); Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Automatic Appeal from the Court of Criminal Appeals Circuit Court for Cocke County. Nos. 5012 and 5040. Ben W. Hooper II, Judge.
State v. Stephenson, 2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 208 (Tenn. Crim. App., Mar. 9, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee) affirming defendant's sentences of death and 60 years in prison, which were imposed during resentencing after defendant was convicted of first-degree murder under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-202(a)(1) (1989) and conspiracy to commit first-degree murder under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-12-103(a) (1989).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for his role in the contract killing of his wife. On appeal, the court held that defendant's sentences of incarceration and death did not constitute multiple punishments for the same conduct because the Blockburger test was satisfied, as first-degree murder required proof of a killing but did not require proof of an argument to commit a killing. Although there was only one victim, defendant committed separate and distinct acts; his act of murder, which he committed by employing another to commit the murder for remuneration or the promise of remuneration, was separate and distinct from defendant's entering into an agreement with his accomplice to have his wife killed. In addition, defendant's agreement with his accomplice to have his wife killed was separate and distinct from the act satisfying the aggravating circumstance of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204(i)(4), defendant's act of offering his accomplice a boat, motor, and pickup truck in exchange for the completed killing. The trial court did not err by allowing the State to read into the record the former testimony of two witnesses because Tenn. R. Evid. 804(b)(1) did not apply to the resentencing hearing.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentences were affirmed.

State v. Housler


No. M2002-00419-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


193 S.W.3d 476; 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 431


February 2, 2006, Session  
May 19, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Housler v. Tennessee, 127 S. Ct. 499, 166 L. Ed. 2d 368, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 8048 (U.S., 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. 11 Appeal by Permission Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Appeal by permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals Circuit Court for Montgomery County. No. 39217. John H. Gasaway, Judge.
State v. Housler, 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 214 (Tenn. Crim. App., Feb. 27, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Circuit Court for Montgomery County (Tennessee) convicting him of four counts of felony murder and sentencing him to life in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for his involvement in the murder of four employees in a fast-food restaurant. On appeal, the court held that the prosecutors' knowing use of his confession, which contained many facts known to be false, did not violate defendant's due process rights because due process merely required the trial court to find that defendant confessed voluntarily and that the confession was minimally corroborated. Once the two conditions were satisfied, the truth or falsity of the confession was a determination for the jury. The trial court found that defendant's confession was voluntary, and defendant did not challenge that finding on appeal. The confession was sufficiently corroborated by numerous witnesses. The court also rejected defendant's argument that the State prosecuted defendant and his accomplice using inconsistent theories, facts, and arguments in violation of his due process rights because defendant's "lone perpetrator" characterization of his accomplice's prosecution was false. The core theory of the two prosecutions was consistent, namely that the accomplice shot the victims and robbed the store while defendant served as a lookout.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentence were affirmed.

Clinton Books, Inc. v. City of Memphis


No. W2003-01300-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


197 S.W.3d 749; 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 313


November 10, 2005, Session  
April 25, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Clinton Books, Inc. v. City of Memphis, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 642 (Tenn., July 21, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed; Remanded to the Trial Court. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals Circuit Court for Shelby County. No. CT-007680-01. Robert A. Lanier, Judge.
Clinton Books, Inc. v. City of Memphis, 2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 724 (Tenn. Ct. App., Nov. 3, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed; Remanded to the Trial Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Shelby County, Tennessee, found that it was without jurisdiction to grant injunctive relief in favor of appellant adult-oriented businesses on a declaratory judgment challenging the constitutionality of Tenn. Code Ann. § 7-51-1402 and seeking an injunction against appellee city to prevent its enforcement. The court of appeals found that the trial court erred in ruling on the constitutional claims. The businesses appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city argued that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to issue a temporary injunction enjoining enforcement of Tenn. Code Ann. § 7-51-1402. The supreme court noted that when the businesses sought an injunction against the enforcement of the statute, they were requesting that the circuit court, acting as a court of equity, enjoin enforcement of a criminal statute. The general rule that courts of equity lacked jurisdiction to enjoin enforcement of a criminal statute that was alleged to be unconstitutional equally applied to the circuit court. The supreme court refused to presume that the State would harass the businesses and their employee by continuing to prosecute them under the statute if it was found to be invalid or inapplicable during the first prosecution brought to trial. The businesses did not present evidence demonstrating that absent the injunction, the value of their property would be destroyed or it would deteriorate. The trial court did not order consolidation or provide notice to the parties of its intent to consolidate the hearings as required by Tenn. R. Civ. P. 65.04(7). The trial court erred in addressing the constitutionality of Tenn. Code Ann. § 7-51-1402.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was affirmed and the case remanded to the trial court for a hearing on the merits with regard to the declaratory judgment action.

Bailey v. County of Shelby


No. W2005-01508-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


188 S.W.3d 539; 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 208


March 21, 2006, Session at Nashville  
March 29, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 29, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Reversed; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reinstated. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals, Western Section Chancery Court for Shelby County. No. CH-04-0550-3. D. J. Alissandratos, Chancellor.
Bailey v. County of Shelby, 2005 Tenn. App. LEXIS 725 (Tenn. Ct. App., Nov. 22, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Reversed; Judgment of the Chancery Court Reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Tennessee Court of Appeals, Western Section, awarded plaintiffs, members of the Shelby County Board of Commissioners, summary judgment on their declaratory judgment action against defendants, County of Shelby, the Shelby County Election Commission, and Shelby County Election Commissioners, that term limits was unauthorized under Tenn. Code Ann. § 5-1-210(4). Defendants sought review pursuant to Tenn. R. App. P. 11.


OVERVIEW: The members argued that Tenn. Code Ann. § 5-1-210(4) did not authorize the imposition of term limits upon members of a county legislative body. The members argued that Tenn. Const. art. VII, § 1 prohibited limiting the number of terms a county legislative official may serve. The supreme court found that there was nothing in the language of the constitution to prevent a county from placing a limit on the number of terms that may be served. The term limits were a qualification for holding office within the meaning of Tenn. Code Ann. § 5-1-210(4). It followed that Shelby County, Tenn., Charter § 2.03(G) was authorized by Tenn. Code Ann. § 5-1-210(4). If the delegates had wanted to prohibit term limits as the members contended, they could have easily added language to that effect. The members did not establish that § 5-1-210(4) was constitutionally defective. The constitution specifically authorized legislation creating different forms of local government, and the General Assembly had very broad powers and discretion in this regard. Defendants' request for an order delaying the election was denied.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was reversed, and the judgment of the chancery court reinstated.

Haley v. Univ. of Tennessee-Knoxville


No. M2005-00998-SC-R23-CQ


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


188 S.W.3d 518; 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 192


January 4, 2006, Session, at Knoxville  
March 17, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected, April 17, 2006.
Motion granted by, Summary judgment denied by, Motion to strike denied by, Dismissed by Haley v. Univ. of Tennessee-Knoxville, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 27282 (E.D. Tenn., Apr. 3, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. Sup. Ct. R. 23 Certified Question of Law Answered. Rule 23 Certified Question of Law United States District Court for the Eastern District of Tennessee. No. 3:30-CV-292. Leon Jordan, Judge.
Haley v. Univ. of Tennessee-Knoxville, 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 803 (Tenn., Oct. 3, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States District Court for the Eastern District of Tennessee certified a question of law to determine whether a voluntary non-suit before the Tennessee Claims Commission (Commission) activated the waiver provision of Tenn. Code Ann. § 9-8-307(b) (2005), barring a federal or state cause of action arising from the same act or omission as the claim before the Commission.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner professor filed a lawsuit against respondent university alleging a violation of Title VII of the Civil Rights Act of 1964, 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000e, based on gender and national origin discrimination. She also alleged a violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The university claimed that the professor's claim for breach of contract filed with the Commission barred her suit in district court, even though the Commission dismissed it without prejudice. The Tennessee Supreme Court determined that, pursuant to Tenn. Sup. Ct. R. 23, it may answer certified questions consistent with the inherent power of the supreme court and with the responsibility to protect the sovereignty of the state. Because Tenn. Code Ann. § 9-8-307(b) provided that the "filing" of a claim operated as a waiver, the fact that the professor's claim was later voluntarily dismissed was irrelevant; the waiver became operational at the time of filing. The supreme court declined to answer additional questions posed by the professor as they were outside the scope of the question certified to the supreme court by the district court.


OUTCOME: The certified question was answered in the affirmative.

State v. Rollins


No. E2003-01811-SC-DDT-DD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


188 S.W.3d 553; 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 191


January 4, 2006, Session  
March 16, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corected March 16, 2006.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Rollins v. Tennessee, 549 U.S. 866, 127 S. Ct. 162, 166 L. Ed. 2d 115, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 6933 (2006)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Rollins v. State, 2012 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 680 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 31, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(a)(1); Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Court of Criminal Appeals Circuit Court for Sullivan County. No. S45,685. R. Jerry Beck, Judge.
State v. Rollins, 2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 373 (Tenn. Crim. App., Apr. 21, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of premeditated murder, felony murder, and especially aggravated robbery and was sentenced to death. The Tennessee Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress his post-presentment statements because they violated his Sixth Amendment right to counsel. The supreme court disagreed. Defendant was meticulously informed by the authorities of his right to counsel and of the consequences of failing to exercise that right before he confessed to the murder. Defendant not only agreed to speak with an officer, but he also signed an advice and waiver of rights form. Furthermore, defendant reviewed the statement and initialed and signed the beginning and end of each page. On two separate occasions defendant elected to forgo the assistance of counsel and instead chose to speak directly to law enforcement officials concerning his role in the murder. Defendant actually requested a second interview with the detectives to clarify his previous statement. Therefore, defendant waived his Sixth Amendment right to counsel and the trial court did not err by refusing to suppress the statements that resulted from the post-presentment interrogations.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Post-conviction relief denied at Rice v. State, 2013 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 282 (Tenn. Crim. App., Mar. 27, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(a)(1); Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals is Affirmed. Automatic Appeal from the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 01-00035. Hon. Joseph B. Dailey, Judge.
State v. Rice, 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 661 (Tenn. Crim. App., July 9, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Court of Criminal Appeals, Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), which convicted him of first-degree murder in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-202 (Supp. 1998) and imposed a death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the first-degree murder of his stepdaughter and sentenced to death. On appeal, the supreme court affirmed, stating that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction and the fact that the murder was committed during the perpetration of a rape. By his own admission, defendant lured the victim into the woods and did not intend for her to leave the woods alive. Once in the woods, the victim was stabbed 16 times and left to die. A jury could have reasonably inferred that defendant's admission to having sex with the victim was his way of explaining any DNA that might have been found on the victim, thereby linking defendant to her rape. His death sentence was appropriate because the proof was sufficient to support the existence of serious physical abuse in violation of Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204(i)(5). In addition to being stabbed 16 times, the victim suffered defensive wounds to her wrist and three of the wounds, those to the neck, were each sufficient to cause her death. Although it was in error to restrict defendant's cross-examination of a witness, that error was harmless.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Rogers


No. M2002-01798-SC-DDT-DD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


188 S.W.3d 593; 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 123


October 5, 2005, Session  
February 17, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Rogers v. Tennessee, 549 U.S. 862, 127 S. Ct. 147, 166 L. Ed. 2d 107, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 6820 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(a)(1); Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Automatic Appeal from the Court of Criminal Appeals Circuit Court for Montgomery County. No. 38939. Robert W. Wedemeyer, Judge.
State v. Rogers, 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 574 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 30, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee) that affirmed his conviction of first-degree premeditated murder, two counts of first-degree felony murder, especially aggravated kidnapping, rape of a child, and two counts of criminal impersonation in connection with the 1996 abduction, rape, and murder of a nine-year-old girl.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the denial of his motion to suppress and the sufficiency of the evidence to support his convictions for first-degree murder, kidnapping, and rape, and to support the aggravating circumstances. The court held that defendant's rights were not violated by the admission of the statements, which were obtained from defendant after he failed a polygraph examination and his status became custodial, because defendant was advised of his Miranda rights and made a knowing and voluntary waiver of those rights earlier in the day and the 5 hours between defendant's waiver of his Miranda rights and his subsequent custodial interrogation did not constitute a significant time lapse. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's first-degree murder conviction where there was no evidence to support his claim that he accidentally ran over the victim because her body showed no signs of trauma and there was no evidence to support his claim that her brother sexually assaulted her. The court also found that defendant's sentence was not arbitrary and that the evidence supported the jury's findings with respect to the four aggravating circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appeals court judgment.

 

110 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Page


No. W2003-01342-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


184 S.W.3d 223; 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 37



February 8, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected, February 8, 2006.
Related proceeding at Page v. State, 2007 Tenn. LEXIS 267 (Tenn., Mar. 5, 2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at Page v. State, 2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 912 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 13, 2011)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at State v. Page, 2017 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 507 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 12, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Reversed. Appeal by permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 99-09509. W. Fred Axley, Judge.
State v. Page, 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 753 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 26, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant had not requested an instruction on facilitation of second degree murder, and none was given. The trial court denied his motion for a new trial in which he had not raised the omission of the instruction on the lesser-included offense of facilitation of second degree murder. The Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee) reversed his conviction for second degree murder. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State asserted that the court of criminal appeals erred in finding Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-18-110(c) unconstitutional because the statute did not preclude lesser-included offense instructions; it merely established reasonable procedures for invoking the right to those instructions. The State urged the Supreme Court of Tennessee to assume that defendant had waived the right to an instruction on facilitation for tactical reasons, a decision which would have bound him. The supreme court concluded that § 40-18-110(c) rendered the omission of the instruction on lesser-included offenses subject to the general rule that issues concerning instructions were considered waived in the absence of objection or a written request, unless they contained plain error. The failure to instruct on lesser-included offenses in the instant case did not constitute plain error. At trial, defendant failed to request a lesser-included offense instruction on facilitation of second degree murder and failed to show that he had not waived that issue for tactical reasons. Therefore, the trial court's failure to instruct on facilitation of second degree murder did not rise to the level of plain error.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of criminal appeals was reversed and defendant's conviction for second degree murder was reinstated. It appearing that defendant was indigent, the costs of the appeal were taxed to the State of Tennessee.

Abdur'Rahman v. Bredesen


No. M2003-01767-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


181 S.W.3d 292; 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 828


June 8, 2005, Session  
October 17, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Abdur'Rahman v. Bredesen, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 3970 (U.S., May 22, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals Chancery Court for Davidson County. No. 02-2236-III. Ellen Hobbs Lyle, Chancellor.
Abdur'Rahman v. Bredesen, 2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 643 (Tenn. Ct. App., Oct. 6, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed a decision of the Court of Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed the trial court's holding that Tennessee's lethal injection protocol was not cruel and unusual punishment in violation of the Eighth Amendment of the United States Constitution or Tenn. Const. art. I, § 16.


OVERVIEW: The inmate filed an action under the Uniform Administrative Procedures Act (UAPA) challenging respondent department of corrections' lethal injection protocol. The court affirmed and held that there was overwhelming evidence that lethal injection was consistent with contemporary standards of decency and that Tennessee's protocol was consistent with the majority of lethal injection protocols used by other states and the federal government. There was testimony that although injection of two of the drugs would alone cause extreme pain, a dosage of a third would cause nearly immediate unconsciousness and that the inmate would feel no pain prior to death. Also, the inmate failed to cite authority or otherwise make a persuasive argument that the adoption of the lethal injection protocol violated procedural due process. The court also held that respondent's disciplinary procedures were not "rules" as defined by the UAPA because they fit squarely into the exceptions under Tenn. Code Ann. § 4-5-102(10)(A), (G). Also the protocol did not violate the Nonlivestock Animal Humane Death Act, and the protocol fell outside the licensing statute applicable to healthcare providers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the court of appeals.

 

112 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


In re C.K.G.


No. M2003-01320-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


173 S.W.3d 714; 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 812


April 15, 2005, Session, Heard at Pulaski 1


1 Oral argument in this case was heard April 15, 2005 in Pulaski, Giles County, Tennessee, as part of this Court's S.C.A.L.E.S. (Supreme Court Advancing Legal Education for Students) project.

 
October 6, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 11; Judgments of the Trial Court and Court of Appeals Vacated in Part; and Affirmed in Part. Appeal by permission from the Court of Appeals, Middle Section. Juvenile Court of Williamson County. No. 38410. Lonnie R. Hoover, Judge.
In re C.K.G., 2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 394 (Tenn. Ct. App., June 22, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Trial Court and Court of Appeals Vacated in Part; and Affirmed in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals, Middle Section (Tennessee), which affirmed the trial court's decision in favor of appellee mother in her action seeking custody and child support of the parties' triplets. The supreme court granted the father's application for permission to appeal.


OVERVIEW: The parties, who were not married, had three children by obtaining eggs donated from an anonymous third-party female, fertilizing the eggs in vitro with the father's sperm, and implanting the fertilized eggs in the mother's uterus. The mother filed a parentage action seeking custody and child support. The trial and appellate courts found in favor of the mother, and the supreme court affirmed on separate grounds, stating that the mother was the children's legal mother with all the rights and responsibilities of parenthood. The court stated that Tennessee's parentage and related statutes did not provide for or control the circumstances of the case. Those statutes simply did not apply to all conceivable parentage determinations. Although giving birth was conspicuously absent from Tennessee's parentage statutes, there was no indication that the General Assembly sought to exclude it as a basis for legal maternity, or even sought to decide questions of maternity at all, Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 36-2-302, 36-2-305, 36-1-102 (2001). Tenn. Code Ann. § 68-3-306 (2001) displayed a policy favoring recognizing gestation and giving birth as a basis for legal maternity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in full the lower courts' judgments concerning comparative fitness, custody, child support, and visitation. The supreme court vacated the appellate court's holding that the father was estopped to deny the mother's maternal status.

Freeman Indus. LLC v. Eastman Chem. Co.


No. E2003-00527-SC-S09-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


172 S.W.3d 512; 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 668; 2005-2 Trade Cas. (CCH) P94,914


May 3, 2005, Session  
August 25, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Freeman Indus. LLC v. Eastman Chem. Co., 2006 Tenn. App. LEXIS 761 (Tenn. Ct. App., Nov. 30, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part; Remanded to the Trial Court. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals Circuit Court for Sullivan County. No. C34355-L. Richard E. Ladd, Chancellor.
Freeman Indus. L.L.C. v. Eastman Chem. Co., 2004 Tenn. App. LEXIS 321 (Tenn. Ct. App., May 18, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part; Remanded to the Trial Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff New York company appealed the judgment from the Court of Appeals (Tennessee), which on review from defendant companies' successful motion to dismiss plaintiff's Tennessee Trade Practices Act (TTPA), Tenn. Code Ann. § 47-25-101 et seq. (2001), claim and their unsuccessful motion for summary judgment on plaintiff's unjust enrichment claim, modified the judgment to hold that the TTPA was not applicable to indirect purchasers.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was an end-user of food products containing sorbates and purchased such products in supermarkets in New York. As an indirect purchaser of sorbates, it filed a lawsuit against defendants, claiming a violation of the TTPA and unjust enrichment, based on defendants' guilty pleas to fixing the prices of sorbates in violation of the Sherman Antitrust Act, 15 U.S.C.S. § 1. The trial court dismissed the claims, and the court of appeals affirmed, adding that the TTPA was not applicable to indirect purchasers such as plaintiff. On review, the court found that contrary to the court of appeals' holding, the plain language of Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 47-25-101 and 47-25-102 (2001) did not prohibit recovery to indirect purchasers who were nonresidents of Tennessee. However, the court found that because defendants' illegal price fixing did not substantially affect Tennessee commerce, it fell outside the scope of the TTPA. Lastly, because plaintiff failed to provide a factual basis to support its bare allegation that any attempt to exhaust its remedies would have been futile, the trial court erred in failing to grant defendants' motion for summary judgment on the unjust enrichment claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the TTPA claim, but modified the judgment to provide that although an indirect purchaser could bring an action under the TTPA, the conduct at issue fell out of the scope of the TTPA. The reversed the judgment denying defendants summary judgment on the unjust enrichment claim and remanded for further proceedings.

 

114 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


City of Knoxville v. Entm't Res., LLC


No. E2002-01143-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


166 S.W.3d 650; 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 606


January 4, 2005, Session  
June 29, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by City of Knoxville v. Entm't Res., LLC, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 9056 (U.S., Dec. 5, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 11. Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals Chancery Court for Knox County. No. 140736-2. Daryl Fansler, Chancellor.
City of Knoxville v. Entm't Res., LLC., 2003 Tenn. App. LEXIS 821 (Tenn. Ct. App., Nov. 21, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city was granted an injunction enjoining appellee adult bookstore from operating its store in alleged violation of the location requirement of Knoxville, Tenn., City Code § 16-468(a). The Court of Appeals of Tennessee, at Knoxville reversed on the grounds that the ordinance's definition of adult bookstores was unconstitutionally vague and the case was remanded for a determination of damages. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parties disputed whether the phrase "substantial or significant portion of its stock and trade," used to define adult bookstores, was impermissibly vague. The supreme court found that it was. First, the inability of the officers charged with enforcing the ordinance to define its key terms weighed heavily against the ordinance's constitutionality. As written, the determination of what constituted a "substantial or significant portion" of a business's "stock and trade" was an entirely subjective one. The ordinance gave no objective guidance to businesses regulated by the ordinance or officials charged with its enforcement. Second, the terms as used in the context of the ordinance could not be defined with any degree of precision. The fact that the terms "substantial" and "significant" were common and familiar terms did not support the argument that they were constitutional as used in the ordinance. Third, the city declined to give any limiting construction to the ordinance, and the supreme court was unable to impose a narrowing definition to salvage its constitutionality. The absence of any ascertainable standard was precisely what offended the Due Process Clause.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was affirmed. The case was remanded to the chancery court to assess the amount of the bookstore's damages and to determine the propriety of awarding attorney's fees as a result of the chancery court's injunction.

Post-conviction relief dismissed at Holton v. State, 201 S.W.3d 626, 2006 Tenn. LEXIS 331 (Tenn., May 4, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(a)(1); Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Automatic Appeal from the Court of Criminal Appeals Circuit Court for Montgomery County. No. 38887. John H. Gasaway, III, Judge.
State v. Reid, 2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1086 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 29, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of two counts of premeditated first degree murder, two counts of especially aggravated kidnapping, and one count of especially aggravated robbery. Defendant was sentenced to death. The Tennessee Court of Appeals affirmed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in finding that he was competent to stand trial. The supreme court disagreed. The trial court held an exhaustive evidentiary hearing and considered the expert testimony of four witnesses. The trial court found that defendant suffered from a brain injury and had difficulties communicating at times. The trial court further found, however, that defendant understood the nature of the proceedings, understood the charges against him, and communicated with his attorneys by suggesting defenses. The fact that not all of defendant's defense strategies or suggestions were pursued did not indicate that he lacked the ability to assist in his defense. In short, the trial court heard the evidence and accredited the testimony of the experts. Therefore, the trial court properly found that defendant was competent to stand trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Ely v. DeRoyal Indus.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Chancery Court for Claiborne County, Tennessee, granted judgment in favor of appellee employer by finding that appellant employee failed to prove her claims of occupational disease or aggravation of pre-existing condition. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee argued that the trial court erred by holding that she could not recover for the aggravation of her lung condition caused by exposure at work. Pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-301, the trial judge found that the employee had not come close in showing that she had an occupational disease in reference to exposure to the chemicals. The appellate court found that the employee did not prove the six elements of an occupational disease by a preponderance of the evidence. There was evidence that the employee's breathing condition existed before working for the employer and was unrelated to any occupational hazard. The medical testimony failed to demonstrate the necessary casual connection between her deteriorating condition and the employer's chemicals. The employee had a severe condition before working. Expert evidence failed to prove the duration and extent of her exposure to specific harmful chemicals was sufficient to cause a permanent aggravation of her pre-existing conditions. Her condition was not typical of occupational injuries. The legislature was within its constitutional authority when it decided to alter the jurisdiction of the general sessions court.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Gomez, 2004 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 144 (Tenn. Crim. App., Feb. 18, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were convicted of conspiracy, facilitation of felony murder, facilitation of especially aggravated robbery, and facilitation of aggravated robbery. The Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee) affirmed. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: One defendant argued, inter alia, that the admission of testimony about an unavailable witness's statement violated his Sixth Amendment right to confront the witnesses against him. The supreme court disagreed. The Crawford error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. The witness's statement did not directly implicate defendant. Immediately after each detective testified about the statement, the trial court provided a cautionary instruction to the jury, limiting the jury's consideration of the testimony about the statement to the issue of whether the conspiracy existed and forbidding its consideration as to whether a particular defendant joined in the charged conspiracy. Moreover, the other properly-admitted evidence of guilt was substantial. An eyewitness identified defendant from a photographic array and again at trial, testifying that she was "very sure" of the identification. Fingerprint evidence placed defendant at the scene, and his girlfriend testified extensively about defendant's involvement in the crime.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Cole


No. W2002-01254-SC-DDT-DD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


155 S.W.3d 885; 2005 Tenn. LEXIS 15


November 9, 2004, Argued  
January 20, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Cole v. Tennessee, 546 U.S. 829, 126 S. Ct. 47, 163 L. Ed. 2d 79, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 6152 (2005)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Cole v. State, 2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 186 (Tenn. Crim. App., Mar. 8, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(a)(1); Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed. Direct Appeal from the Court of Criminal Appeals. Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 01-01221. Joseph B. Dailey, Judge.
State v. Cole, 2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1002 (Tenn. Crim. App., Nov. 24, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first degree premeditated murder and sentenced to death. The Tennessee Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction. The supreme court disagreed. The proof offered at trial showed that defendant directed the victim to drive him to an overgrown area behind an apartment complex to obtain drugs. Defendant became upset because the victim was unable to pay immediately a fifteen-dollar debt that the victim owed defendant. Defendant pointed the gun at the victim, told the victim to open his mouth, and then shot the victim first above the victim's left eye and then again behind the victim's left ear. By his own admission, defendant shot the victim a second time, with the gun within one inch of the victim's head, to ensure the victim's death. Defendant's statements after the crime indicated that he thought about shooting the victim before doing so. Defendant told the police that he had committed the murder because the victim owed him money that he needed to support his pregnant girlfriend and because the victim had disrespected him. Those statements supported the jury's finding of premeditation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Howell v. State


No. W2003-01056-SC-R11-PD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


151 S.W.3d 450; 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 958


April 7, 2004, Session  
November 16, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Howell v. Tennessee, 544 U.S. 985, 125 S. Ct. 1855, 161 L. Ed. 2d 742, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 3114 (2005)
Appeal after remand at, Post-conviction relief denied at Howell v. State, 2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 447 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 14, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Permission to Appeal; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals is Reversed and Remanded. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals. Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. P-14334. Hon. Otis Higgs, Jr., Judge.
Howell v. State, 1997 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1225 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 3, 1997)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed a decision of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed the trial court's denial of the inmate's motion to reopen his petition for post-conviction relief that alleged that the inmate was mentally retarded under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-203(a) (2003), and therefore ineligible for the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was sentenced to death. A psychologist testified that the inmate's level of intellectual functioning was within the retarded range of intelligence. The court held: (1) Section 39-13-203(a) (2003) was not intended to apply to a "range" of IQ scores; (2) the inmate's motion should be reviewed applying the colorable claim standard; (3) the inmate was confronted with circumstances beyond his control that prevented him from previously challenging his conviction and sentence on constitutional grounds. For these reasons, the court found the individual's individual interests to outweigh those of the State under the specific facts; (4) applying the "clear and convincing" burden of proof to petitioners, such as the inmate, who were for the first time, in a petition for post-conviction relief or a motion to reopen post-conviction proceedings, able to raise a claim of mental retardation to avoid capital punishment violated their due process rights at an evidentiary hearing. Therefore, the inmate would have the opportunity to prove mental retardation by preponderance of the evidence; and (5) the inmate was not entitled to a jury determination of mental retardation.


OUTCOME: The court held that the inmate was entitled to an evidentiary hearing on the issue of mental retardation and at the hearing he would have the opportunity to prove mental retardation by a preponderance of the evidence.

 

122 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Denton


No. E2000-02615-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


149 S.W.3d 1; 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 935



November 15, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected November 19, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Application for Permission to Appeal; Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part, and Remanded. Appeal by permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals, Criminal Court of McMinn County Nos. 98-535 to 98-539, 98-694 to 98-705, 99-244, 99-246 R. Steven Bebb, Judge.
State v. Denton, 2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 907 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 28, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of one count of sexual battery by an authority figure, six counts of sexual battery, and three counts of assault. The Tennessee Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in joining several counts in a single action. The supreme court agreed. Because the offenses were not "signature" crimes or part of a larger, continuing plan or conspiracy, the offenses alleged against defendant did not constitute a common scheme or plan and the trial court erred in denying the defendant's motion to sever the offenses for trial. The offenses were not so factually unique or distinctive as to constitute defendant's modus operandi. While there were certainly similarities among the allegations, those similarities were simply that all of the incidents were sexual assaults by a physician against a patient. Even though defendant was alleged to have touched the women in a sexual manner while examining them in his office, the circumstances of each encounter were not so unique and distinctive as to allow one to conclude that if defendant committed one offense, then he also must have committed the other offenses as well. Therefore, the offenses did not evidence a distinctive design nor were they "signature" crimes of defendant.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were reversed. The case was remanded for new trials.

 

123 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Robinson


No. W2001-01299-SC-R11-DD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


146 S.W.3d 469; 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 843


June 2, 2004, Argued  
September 28, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Robinson, 2004 Tenn. LEXIS 912 (Tenn., Nov. 1, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Robinson v. Tennessee, 546 U.S. 1214, 126 S. Ct. 1429, 164 L. Ed. 2d 132, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 1839 (2006)
Post-conviction relief denied at Robinson v. State, 2013 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 251 (Tenn. Crim. App., Mar. 20, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Tenn. R. App. P. 11. Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Reversed in Part and Affirmed in Part; Judgment of the Trial Court Reinstated. Appeal by Permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 97-13179-80. James C. Beasley, Jr., Judge.
State v. Robinson, 2003 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 694 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 13, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed in Part and Affirmed in Part; Judgment of the Trial Court Reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed an application for permission to appeal a judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Criminal Court for Shelby County (Tennessee), which reversed defendant's conviction for premeditated first-degree murder and his sentence of death. Defendant had also been convicted of especially aggravated kidnapping.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that the trial court erred by failing to instruct the jury on facilitation and solicitation of first-degree premeditated murder and especially aggravated kidnapping. The court held that the appellate court erred in reversing defendant's conviction and sentence because the trial court had not erred by failing to instruct the jury on facilitation and solicitation. The evidence unmistakably established either the completed offenses of murder and especially aggravated kidnapping or defendant's claim of innocence. No reasonable jury could have concluded from the evidence presented that defendant had the knowledge required for facilitation but lacked the intent required for criminal responsibility. The trial court did not err by permitting the medical examiner to display the victim's cleaned and reconstructed skull as a demonstrative aid during his testimony because defendant failed to show unfair prejudice that outweighed the evidence's probative value. The State did not present inconsistent theories and evidence in the separate trials of defendant and a codefendant. Finally, the sentence of death was not disproportionate or excessive.


OUTCOME: With respect to issues not specifically addressed in the court's opinion, the appellate court's judgment was affirmed. The court reversed the appellate court's reversal of defendant's conviction. The court reinstated the judgment of the trial court.
