PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Court of Criminal Appeals. Criminal Court for Shelby County. Nos. 94-02797-99 and 95-1128-29, Joseph B. Dailey, Judge.
State v. Carruthers, 1999 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1333 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 21, 1999)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(a), pro se defendant and represented co-defendant appealed from an order of the Tennessee Court of Criminal Appeals, which affirmed their Shelby County Criminal Court convictions of first degree murder and their death sentences, raising numerous procedural, statutory, and constitutional errors.


OVERVIEW: Pro se defendant and represented co-defendant were each convicted of three counts of first degree murder, three counts of especially aggravated kidnapping and one count of especially aggravated robbery. Based on extensive evidence, the jury found numerous aggravating circumstances under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-204(2), (5), (7), and (12) (Supp. 1994) and imposed death. On direct appeal, the Court of Criminal Appeals affirmed both defendant's and co-defendant's convictions and sentences. Pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-206(a), the Supreme Court of Tennessee reviewed the record and affirmed the judgment against defendant, holding, inter alia, that defendant, by his extreme and egregious misconduct, implicitly waived and forfeited his right to counsel under U.S. Const. amend. VI. The appellate court further held, under its proportionality review of capital cases, that the sentences of death upon pro se defendant were not excessive or imposed in an arbitrary manner. However, the appellate court reversed co-defendant's convictions and remanded for a new trial, holding that the trial court's failure to grant a severance resulted in prejudicial error.


OUTCOME: Pro se defendant's convictions for first degree murder and sentences of death were affirmed; the trial court did not abuse its discretion in finding that defendant, through his conduct, waived his right to counsel. Co-defendant's convictions and sentences were reversed and the case remanded for a new trial because co-defendant's right to a fair trial was prejudiced when he was denied severance.

 

165 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Ferrell v. Cigna Prop. & Cas. Ins. Co.


No. M1999-01669-WC-R3-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


33 S.W.3d 731; 2000 Tenn. LEXIS 686



December 8, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Circuit Court for Warren County. No. 9962 Richard McGregor, Clerk and Master.



DISPOSITION: Circuit Court Affirmed as Modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Warren County (Tennessee) which found that he had failed to meet the statute of limitations on his workers' compensation claim, and that his hearing loss was not work-related.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee had a hearing problem since he was a child. His hearing loss became more serious when he started working for appellee company as a bulldozer operator and then as foreman on construction sites where he was exposed to loud noise from machinery and explosives. After he stopped working for appellee, his attorney counseled him to file suit on the theory that his hearing loss might be work-related. The trial court ruled that appellant's suit was barred by the statute of limitations, and that appellant's injury was not work-related. The appellate court affirmed, but modified the judgment. Appellant had no actual knowledge that his condition was work-related until after he filed his complaint, which satisfied the statute of limitations. However, the court found the presence of a long-standing diagnosis of one condition and a recent diagnosis of a different condition puzzling. Under the circumstances, it could not say that the evidence preponderated against the trial court's findings that the injury was not work-related. Additionally, an improper procedure for referring the workers' compensation case to the clerk and master was used, but was not reversible.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as modified. As appellant learned that his injury was work-related the day before trial, the statute of limitations had not expired. However, the court could not say that the evidence preponderated against the findings of the trial court regarding causation of the injury. Although the proper procedure was not followed when the clerk and master was appointed, it was not reversible error.

Tucker v. Foamex


No. W1999-01547-SC-R3-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


31 S.W.3d 241; 2000 Tenn. LEXIS 617



November 6, 2000, Decided  
November 6, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Chancery Court for Gibson County. No. 13880. George R. Ellis, Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer appealed the judgment of the Chancery Court for Gibson County (Tennessee), awarding plaintiff employee benefits for permanent partial disability beyond his 65th birthday in a workers' compensation case.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff worker was injured at age 59. He was treated for his injury and reached maximum medical improvement after he turned 60. The trial court found plaintiff was 92 percent permanently partially disabled and awarded 368 weeks of benefits under Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6- 207(3)(F). Plaintiff was to receive benefits for almost 2 years after his 65th birthday. Defendant employer alleged that Tenn. Code Ann. § 50-6-207(4)(A)(i) applied and limited the number of weeks for payment from the date of maximum medical improvement to plaintiff's 65th birthday. The court found that because plaintiff was not over the age of 60 on the date of injury but was within 400 weeks of his 65th birthday when benefits for permanent partial disability became payable, the trial court applied the correct statute in awarding benefits and the benefits were payable beyond plaintiff's 65th birthday.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as the trial court based its award for permanent partial disability to the body as a whole on the correct statute and plaintiff was not limited to benefits payable only until the age of 65.

Halbert v. Shelby County Election Comm'n


No. W1998-00706-SC-R3-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


31 S.W.3d 246; 2000 Tenn. LEXIS 618



November 6, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the Chancery Court for Shelby County. No. 98-0698-2. Floyd Peete, Jr., Chancellor.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Chancery Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision of the Chancery Court for Shelby County (Tennessee) denying her request for declaratory and injunctive relief brought on the grounds that her election opponent was not eligible to serve on the Board of Education of the Memphis City Schools.


OVERVIEW: Appellant filed this action contending that her opponent in an election for a seat on the Board of Education of the Memphis City Schools (Board) was not eligible to serve on the Board. Appellant sought declaratory and injunctive relief. The trial court denied relief to appellant and, on appeal, the court affirmed. The term "resident voter" as used in the Board's charter provision establishing the eligibility requirements for service on the Board required the candidate to possess the legal qualifications which would entitle him or her to vote in the election if registered. Appellant's opponent qualified as a "resident voter" as that term was defined, such that he was eligible to serve on the Board.


OUTCOME: Trial court's decision was affirmed. Appellant's election opponent qualified as "resident voter" as term was used in provision setting forth qualifications for election to Board of Education of the Memphis City Schools, as he possessed qualifications entitling him to vote if registered.

 

168 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


State v. Culbreath


No. W1999-01553-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


30 S.W.3d 309; 2000 Tenn. LEXIS 588



October 20, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal By Permission from the Court of Criminal Appeals. Criminal Court for Shelby County. Nos. 96-13497, 97-00667, -72, -73, -75. L.T. Lafferty, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Reversed In Part; Judgment of the Trial Court Reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged a decision from the Tennessee Court of Criminal Appeals, in which it was agreed that a private attorney hired to investigate and prosecute obscenity cases had a conflict of interest, but in which the court refused to dismiss the indictments against the defendants.


OVERVIEW: A private attorney was approached by the executive director of an organization who asked him to meet with two assistant district attorneys, regarding the prosecution of obscenity cases. After the attorney spent a significant amount of time investigating and was compensated for his time, charges were brought against the defendants. The court agreed that the private attorney had an actual conflict of interest. He was privately compensated by a special interest group and thus owed a duty of loyalty to that group, at the same time, he was serving in the role of public prosecutor and owed the duty of loyalty attendant to that office. The defendants' liberty interests in the case were obviously significant, as they had been charged with multiple felony offenses. The private attorney's conflict of interest tainted the entire prosecution of the case well before the charges were presented to the grand jury. Dismissal of the indictments was the appropriate remedy to redress the constitutional error.


OUTCOME: Dismissal of indictments against defendants was appropriate. The entire case was tainted by private attorney's conflict of interest, who was acting as a special prosecutor.

State v. Keen

Post-conviction relief denied at Keen v. State, 2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 442 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 5, 2006)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Application denied by Keen v. State, 2011 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 972 (Tenn. Crim. App., June 29, 2011)
Decision reached on appeal by Keen v. State, 2017 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 710 (Tenn. Crim. App., Aug. 11, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Automatic Appeal from the Court of Criminal Appeals. Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 90-06629. Hon. John P. Colton, Judge.
State v. Keen, 1999 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 123 (Tenn. Crim. App., Feb. 10, 1999)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An order from the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), affirming appellant's sentence of death after he pleaded guilty to first degree murder in perpetration of the rape of an eight-year-old girl, was automatically appealed.


OVERVIEW: A jury sentenced appellant to death for the murder of a child. On automatic appeal from the appeals court, the sentence was affirmed. The evidence amply supported the two aggravating circumstances found by the jury, and any mitigating circumstances were outweighed beyond a reasonable doubt. Appellant was not entitled to an instruction on the life imprisonment without possibility of parole because his offense was committed before the effective date of the act amending the capital sentencing statutes to provide for that sentence, and there was no constitutional impediment to the legislature's discretion. Although the court found technical error in the jury instruction regarding the weighing of circumstantial evidence, the error did not affirmatively affect the outcome of the hearing given that the jury could not have arrived at a contrary conclusion using the appellant's proposed instruction. Finally, the court compared the nature of the crime and the circumstances of the appellant with other cases in which the death penalty was imposed and affirmed, and concluded the sentence of death was neither arbitrarily nor disproportionately applied.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Crime was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel under torture or serious physical abuse prongs and both aggravating circumstances were present and outweighed any mitigating circumstances. Appellant was not deprived of unanimous jury verdict. The constitution did not require an instruction on life without parole. Death sentence was neither disproportionate nor arbitrarily applied.

 

170 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Planned Parenthood of Middle Tenn. v. Sundquist


No. M1996-00060-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


38 S.W.3d 1; 2000 Tenn. LEXIS 515



September 15, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected March 15, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals, Middle Section Circuit Court for Davidson County. No. 92C-1672. Hamilton V. Gayden, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Tenn. R. App. P. 11 Appeal by Permission; Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed in Part and Reversed in Part; Case Remanded to Trial Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After striking certain parts of abortion statutes for unconstitutionally imposing an undue burden on a woman's right to choose abortion, the Tennessee Court of Appeals upheld the following provisions: the waiting period requirement, certain informed consent provisions, and the second trimester hospitalization requirement. Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-15-202(d)(1), (b)(1)-(3), (b)(5)-(c), and -201(c)(2). Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: Seeking declaratory and injunctive relief, plaintiffs filed suit alleging, inter alia, that certain provisions of Tennessee's criminal abortion statutes violated a woman's right to privacy under both the state and federal constitutions. Applying the undue burden standard, the lower court struck certain provisions (e.g., that the attending physician inform the woman that "abortion in a considerable number of cases constitutes a major surgical procedure"), but upheld the waiting period requirement, the second trimester hospitalization requirement, and the remaining informed consent provisions. Finding that a woman's right to terminate her pregnancy was a fundamental right to privacy guaranteed by the Tennessee Constitution, the court applied strict scrutiny to hold that the second trimester hospitalization requirement, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-15-201(c)(2), the informed consent and physician-only counseling requirements, § 39-15-202(b)-(c), the mandatory waiting period requirement, § 39-15-202(d)(1), and the medical emergency exceptions, § 39-15-202(d)(3), -202(g), were unconstitutional because the statutes were not narrowly tailored to further compelling state interests.


OUTCOME: Applying strict scrutiny rather than the less exacting undue burden standard, the court partially affirmed and reversed the lower court's decision by holding that challenged provisions of Tennessee's criminal abortion statutes violated a woman's fundamental right to privacy under the Tennessee Constitution because the state failed to prove that the statutes were narrowly tailored to further compelling state interests. Remanded to trial court.

State v. Jefferson


No. M1997-00115-SC-R11-PC


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


31 S.W.3d 558; 2000 Tenn. LEXIS 457



August 25, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 25, 2000.
Post-conviction relief denied at Jefferson v. State, 2005 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 139 (Tenn. Crim. App., Feb. 16, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for Davidson County. Walter C. Kurtz, Judge. No. 92-C-1372.
State v. Jefferson, 1998 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1329 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 31, 1998)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment in the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), which affirmed the trial court judgment overruling defendant's motion for a new trial on guilt or innocence before resentencing defendant to life imprisonment for first degree premeditated murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was re-indicted and tried for premeditated murder. The jury, pursuant to instruction, returned a guilty verdict and sentenced defendant to 40 years' imprisonment. Because the sentencing statute had been declared unconstitutional, the only legal sentence on a conviction for first degree murder was life imprisonment. The State moved to correct judgment; the trial court granted the motion and modified the sentence to life imprisonment. The court found the trial court lacked authority to change the jury's verdict, and ordered a new trial on punishment alone; that jury imposed life imprisonment. The court affirmed, finding that, while the appellate court should have remanded the case for a new trial, the decision was not manifestly unjust. The jury had the opportunity to convict defendant of second degree murder, and evidence overwhelmingly support the first degree conviction. The case, therefore, did not fall under the second exception to the law of the case doctrine.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. The appellate court properly affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion for a new trial. The case did not fall under the second exception to the law of the case doctrine. While the appellate court erred in remanding for a new trial on punishment alone, the error was not manifestly unjust.

Penley v. Honda Motor Co.


No. W1998-00765-SC-R11-CV


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


31 S.W.3d 181; 2000 Tenn. LEXIS 458; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P15,890



August 25, 2000, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 25, 2000.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal by Permission from the Court of Appeals, Western Section. Circuit Court for Chester County. Hon. Whit LaFon, Judge. No. 4196.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals is Affirmed; Case Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed the judgment of the Court of Appeals, Western Section (Tennessee), which affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to defendants, in a suit to determine whether the Tennessee Products Liability Act's 10-year statute of repose, Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-28-103(a) (1980 & Supp. 1999), was tolled when the plaintiff suffered temporary mental incompetency.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to defendants, and it held that the Tennessee Products Liability Act's 10-year statute of repose, Tenn. Code Ann. § 29-28-103(a) (1980 & Supp. 1999), was not tolled by a plaintiff's physical or mental incompetence. The appellate court also held that the absence of a tolling provision for persons of unsound mind did not render § 29-28-103(a) unconstitutional under the Tennessee Constitution. Plaintiff appealed. First, the court concluded that the failure of the legislature to expressly include any provision exempting persons of unsound mind from § 29-28-103(a) strongly indicated its desire not to have such an exemption. Second, the language of the legal disability statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 28-1-106 (1980 & Supp. 1999), strongly suggested that it only applied to toll statutes of limitations. Third, a policy that allowed a plaintiff's mental incompetency to toll a statute of repose would have severely damaged the purposes underlying statutes of repose generally because it envisioned no practical end to a defendant's liability. Consequently, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment was affirmed. The legislature did not expressly include any provision exempting persons of unsound mind from the Tennessee Products Liability Act's 10-year statute of repose, this strongly indicated its desire not to have such an exemption; and the legal disability statute's language strongly suggested that it only applied to toll, not statutes of repose, but statutes of limitations.

State v. Morris

Post-conviction relief denied at Morris v. State, 2006 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 782 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 10, 2006)

State v. Morris, 1999 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 96 (Tenn. Crim. App., Feb. 5, 1999)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Criminal Appeals Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, convicted of two counts of premeditated first degree murder and one count of aggravated rape in the Criminal Court for Madison County, Tennessee, appealed his death sentence for one of the murders which was found to have two aggravating circumstances: the murder was especially heinous, atrocious or cruel, and the murder was committed in the course of any first degree murder, rape, burglary or kidnapping.


OVERVIEW: The defendant was convicted of two counts of premeditated first degree murder and one count of aggravated rape. The jury imposed the death penalty and life without parole for the murders and a 25-year sentence for the rape. The jury found evidence of two aggravating circumstances; that the murder was especially heinous, atrocious or cruel and it was committed in the course of any first degree murder, rape, burglary or kidnapping; which outweighed evidence of mitigation beyond a reasonable doubt. The appeals court affirmed. Upon automatic review, the Tennessee Supreme Court concluded that the evidence was sufficient to support the murder verdicts and that the defendant was not entitled to relief on the issue of whether electrocution was cruel and unusual punishment. The court also held that the death sentence was not arbitrary, excessive or disproportionate to sentences imposed in cases involving similar crimes and defendants, and affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. The evidence supported the jury's findings of two aggravating circumstances, that these aggravating circumstances outweighed mitigating evidence beyond a reasonable doubt, and that the death sentence was not arbitrary, excessive, or disproportionate. The defendant was not entitled to relief on the issue of whether electrocution was cruel and unusual punishment because lethal injection was the default mode of execution.

ATS Southeast, Inc. v. Carrier Corp.


No. M1999-02658-SC-R23-CQ


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


18 S.W.3d 626; 2000 Tenn. LEXIS 245



May 12, 2000, Decided

DISPOSITION: Certification of Questions of State Law from Federal Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States District Court for the Middle District of Tennessee certified a question regarding whether a corporation had standing to bring a private cause of action for treble damages pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 47-18-109(a).


OVERVIEW: The court accepted certification of whether a corporation had standing to bring a private cause of action for treble damages pursuant to Tenn. Code Ann. § 47-18-109(a). Petitioners filed a breach of contract action against respondent corporation; respondent filed a counterclaim against petitioners and petitioners' predecessors, seeking treble damages. The Tennessee Consumer Protection Act (Act), Tenn. Code Ann. § 47-18-102(b) protected business and consumers from unfair or deceptive acts or practices affecting the conduct of any trade or commerce. Prior to the amendment of the Act, corporations were disallowed from pursuing treble damages. The Act, as amended in 1989, Tenn. Code Ann. § 47-18-109(a) defined a person to include a corporation. The language of Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 47-10-109(a) and 47-18-103(7) was clear and unambiguous. The two statutes indicated that corporations had standing to bring a private cause of action for treble damages under the Tennessee Consumer Protection Act.


OUTCOME: Tennessee Consumer Protection Act clearly contemplated that corporations injured by a violation of the statute should be granted standing; corporations had standing to bring a private cause of action for treble damages under the statute.

State v. Sledge

SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON

March 20, 2000, Filed

DISPOSITION: COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After being sentenced to death for a first degree felony murder conviction, defendant appealed a judgment from the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee) remanding the case for resentencing.


OVERVIEW: The Tennessee Supreme Court granted review to address whether omission of a culpable mental state in an indictment for felony murder rendered the indictment insufficient to support a conviction for first degree felony murder. The court held specific reference to a statute within the indictment may be sufficient to place the accused on notice of the charged offense. The indictment provided ample information to protect the defendant from reprosecution for the same offense. The court concluded that recklessness, knowledge, or intent could be inferred from the conduct alleged in the indictment--that the defendant unlawfully killed the victim during the perpetration of the aggravated robbery.


OUTCOME: Remanded to the trial court for resentencing. Inclusion in the language of the indictment of the explicit reference to the felony murder statutory section was sufficient to appraise the defendant of his charge and to protect the defendant from reprosecution for the same offense.

State v. Walker

SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


12 S.W.3d 460; 2000 Tenn. LEXIS 67

DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS IS REVERSED; JUDGMENT OF THE TRIAL COURT IS REINSTATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Court of Criminal Appeals (Tennessee), finding that both the custodial arrest of defendant and the subsequent search were constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was driving a car with the radio noticeably high. Defendant was approached by a police officer who asked defendant for his driver's license and vehicle registration. Defendant failed to produce either, but gave the officer all the information. Although the information was verified by the dispatcher, the officer decided to take him into custody for violating the noise ordinance. The officer searched defendant and found marijuana and a substance containing cocaine. The officer testified that he would have given defendant a citation and released him but defendant did not have his driver's license or other identification with him. The State presented no evidence of an objective reason to doubt the reliability of the information given by defendant. This court found that under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-7-118(c)(3), the officer wrongly placed defendant under custodial arrest. Because the custodial arrest was unlawful, the search incident to the arrest was also unlawful, and the seized evidence must be suppressed.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; because the custodial arrest was unlawful, the search incident to the arrest was also unlawful, and the seized evidence must be suppressed.

State v. Darden


NO. M1996-00044-SC-R11-CD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, MIDDLE SECTION, AT NASHVILLE


12 S.W.3d 455; 2000 Tenn. LEXIS 56



February 7, 2000, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] CIRCUIT COURT. ROBERTSON COUNTY. HON. ROBERT W. WEDEMEYER.
State v. Darden, 1997 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1101 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 30, 1997)
State v. Morrow, 1998 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 1299 (Tenn. Crim. App., Dec. 22, 1998)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Appeals of Robertson County (Tennessee) that affirmed his convictions for felony murder, civil rights intimidation, and attempted kidnapping after his case was transferred from juvenile to adult court under the Tennessee transfer statute, Tenn. Code Ann. § 37-1-134 (Supp. 1999).


OVERVIEW: Juvenile defendant was transferred to adult court under Tenn. Code Ann. § 37-1-134 (Supp. 1999) and convicted of felony murder, civil rights intimidation, and attempted kidnapping. Appellate court affirmed the convictions, and defendant appealed, claiming the trial court did not have jurisdiction over the charges because they were not addressed at the transfer hearing. The supreme court affirmed appellate court's ruling. It held that defendant was properly transferred under § 37-1-134 because the trial court had reasonable grounds to believe that defendant committed the crimes with which he was charged. Additionally, the trial court had jurisdiction over felony murder because premeditated murder was addressed in the transfer order. Felony murder and premeditated murder were different ways of committing the same crime, first-degree murder. The other charges were subject to trial court's jurisdiction because they were properly characterized as subsequent criminal charges in the transfer statute.


OUTCOME: State supreme court affirmed juvenile defendant's convictions for felony murder, civil rights intimidation, and attempted kidnapping because defendant was properly transferred to adult court under the Tennessee transfer statute, and all charges were addressed at the transfer hearing.

 

180 of 1427 DOCUMENTS


Workman v. State


S.Ct. No. M1999-01334-SC-DPE-PD


SUPREME COURT OF TENNESSEE, WESTERN SECTION, AT JACKSON


22 S.W.3d 807; 2000 Tenn. LEXIS 655



January 3, 2000, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The cause came to be heard upon the motion of the State requesting an execution date be set. Respondent filed a response to motion to set execution date and motion for certificate of commutation, alleging he was convicted upon perjured testimony and was not guilty of capital murder.


OVERVIEW: The State argued respondent was not entitled to further delay in the imposition of his sentence of death and his case was not an appropriate one for the court to consider issuance of a certificate of commutation. All members of the court agreed that there is no legal basis why an execution date should not be set. The respondent had unsuccessfully challenged his conviction and sentence through direct appeal to the court and had unsuccessfully pursued state post-conviction and federal habeas corpus remedies. He had exhausted the standard three-tier appeals process. There existed no procedure, no method, and no means by which the conviction or the sentence could be further tested or scrutinized under the procedural guidelines within which the court functioned. His case was therefore ripe for the setting of an execution date. Accordingly, the State's motion to set an execution date was granted and the execution date set.


OUTCOME: The motion for certificate of commutation was denied; the State's motion to set an execution date was granted. The record supported both the conviction and sentence. The respondent presented no extenuating circumstances that warranted issuance of a certificate of commutation.

Matthews v. State


No. M2015-02422-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2016 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 941


October 18, 2016, Session 
December 21, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Matthews v. State, 2017 Tenn. LEXIS 232 (Tenn., Apr. 13, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 3 [*1] Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2009-D-3252. Mark J. Fishburn, Judge.
State v. Moody, 2013 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 396 (Tenn. Crim. App., May 9, 2013)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Under the Sixth Amendment, Tenn. Const. art. I, § 9, and Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 40-30-103, 40-30-110(f) (2014), defendant's petition for post-conviction relief was properly denied as counsel was not ineffective for failing to call a co-defendant as a witness at trial because counsel testified that she had no reason to believe that the co-defendant would testify on behalf of defendant after his attorney announced in court that the co-defendant refused to testify, and she did not believe his testimony would help the defense; and she was not ineffective in her explanation of felony murder as counsel said she believed defendant understood the concepts of felony murder and criminal responsibility; and there was no support in the record that defendant's lack of understanding could be attributed to counsel's failure to explain and review those concepts with him.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

In re A-River City Bail Bond, Inc.


No. W2015-01578-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2016 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 925


April 12, 2016, Assigned on Briefs 
December 12, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 3 [*1] Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. (No Number Assigned). Lee V. Coffee, Presiding Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Shelby County, Tenn., R. 7 applied to appellant bondsman engaging in that business before the Rule's effective date because Shelby County, Tenn., R. 7.11 said it applied to all bondsmen, it was not arbitrary or capricious, and it was within the trial court's province; [2]-Suspending the bondsman's protected right to write bail bonds did not violate due process because he was sufficiently apprised of its reasons, as his motion to set it aside correctly stated its reason, which the court's conversation with his counsel confirmed, and he had a sufficient opportunity to be heard, under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-11-125(b) and Shelby County, Tenn., R. 7.10, as between the suspension and his hearing and between the hearing and an order denying his motion to set the suspension aside, he did not remedy the known reason for the suspension, so these delays were not unreasonable.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Hampton

COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2016 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 883


July 12, 2016, Assigned on Briefs 
November 23, 2016, Filed

DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-While defendants' sentences, making them eligible for parole after about 29 and 38 years, were lengthy, they were not the functional equivalent of a sentence of life without parole, allowing one defendant to be eligible for parole at about age 45 and the other at about age 55 and thus, they did not violate the Eighth Amendment; [2]-Defendants' challenges to the length of their sentences based on the enhancement and mitigation factors failed, as the trial court specifically noted it was considering the principles and purposes of sentencing and the applicable factors, including that first defendant was a leader and second defendant had previously engaged in animal cruelty when he shot a dog for pleasure or excitement; [3]-Second defendant's consecutive sentences under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-115, were supported by the trial court's finding that he was a dangerous offender.


OUTCOME: Affirmed and remanded.

DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:

State v. Welch

DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Circuit Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The affidavit in support of the search warrant sufficiently established probable cause for the search, as the observations by the cooperating individuals were corroborated by the detectives prior to the search warrant being applied for when detectives followed the pills from the cooperating individuals to defendants; [2]-While the warrantless entry into defendants' home was unlawful, the evidence was properly seized as a result of a valid warrant based on evidence developed independently of any information gained from the warrantless entry; [3]-Because the trial court properly considered the evidence, stated what enhancement and mitigating factors were considered, and complied with the purposes and principles of sentencing, it did not abuse its discretion in enhancing defendant's sentence and imposing within range sentences.

State v. Conkin


No. E2015-01286-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2016 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 669


June 29, 2016, Session 
September 7, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 3 [*1] Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Sullivan County. No. S62723. James F. Goodwin, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The evidence was sufficient to support defendant's DUI conviction under Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-10-401(1) where it showed that she was found asleep in the driver's seat of a running vehicle with the back-up and brake lights illuminated, the officer testified she had a very lethargic demeanor after he woke her, she performed poorly on field sobriety tests, she admitted to having taken multiple prescription medications the night before, and she had exhibited an ability to direct the use of the vehicle by unlocking it, turning the heat on, and rolling down the window; [2]-The trial court did not err by denying defendant's motion to suppress evidence seized after the officer seized defendant because the officer's actions were justified under the community caretaking doctrine, given that defendant was asleep in the running vehicle.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Russell v. State


No. M2015-02101-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT NASHVILLE


2016 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 624


April 19, 2016, Assigned on Briefs 
August 22, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief dismissed at Russell v. State, 2016 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 769 (Tenn. Crim. App., Oct. 13, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 3 [*1] Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Davidson County. No. 2002-I-1192. Mark J. Fishburn, Judge.
Russell v. State, 2012 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 696 (Tenn. Crim. App., Sept. 5, 2012)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether defendant was entitled to postconviction relief. HOLDINGS: [1]-Although defendant contended that his postconviction claims were not time-barred, under Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-30-102(b)(1), because they were brought within one year of a federal opinion, which he contended established a new constitutional right requiring retroactive application, regardless of whether the opinion established a constitutional right not recognized at the time of defendant's criminal proceeding or whether retrospective application was required, defendant's arguments did not present a colorable claim for postconviction relief, under Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 40-30-103 and 40-30-106(f), because the Tennessee statute at issue, Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-16-603(b)(3), was not void for vagueness, as it clearly required gauging the riskiness of conduct in which a defendant engaged on a particular occasion.


OUTCOME: Dismissal affirmed.

State v. Clayton


No. W2015-00158-CCA-R3-DD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2016 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 614


March 1, 2016, Session 
August 18, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by State v. Clayton, 2017 Tenn. LEXIS 723 (Tenn., Nov. 20, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 3 [*1] Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part; Case Remanded. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 1203160. Carolyn W. Blackett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part; Case Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Absent evidence of when the judicial determination of probable cause occurred, the appellate court could not conclude that the delay in making a probable cause determination after defendant's arrest was unreasonable and in violation of the Fourth Amendment, and the record did not show that the delay was motivated by ill will against defendant; [2]-Dual convictions for possession of a firearm with the intent to go armed during the commission of a dangerous felony and employing a firearm in the commission or attempt to commit a dangerous felony violated double jeopardy principles; [3]-The trial court did not abuse its discretion in allowing the State to introduce photos depicting the face of each victim, as they were relevant to establishing the mass murder aggravating circumstance, were not unduly gruesome, and the number of photos was limited to one for each victim.


OUTCOME: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.

Jones v. State


No. W2015-01481-CCA-R3-PC


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2016 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 595


March 1, 2016, Session 
August 11, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Jones v. State, 2016 Tenn. LEXIS 779 (Tenn., Oct. 21, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 3 [*1] Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 1006236. James C. Beasley, Jr., Judge.
State v. Jones, 2013 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 169 (Tenn. Crim. App., Feb. 27, 2013)



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Petitioner was not entitled to postconviction relief on his claim that his trial counsel was ineffective for failing to file a motion to suppress evidence as a result of police questioning and collection of DNA evidence from him on the day after the victim's body was discovered where the totality of proof showed that a reasonable person in petitioner's position would not have thought that he was under arrest, as from the beginning of the encounter petitioner indicated his desire to talk to the police and accompanied them voluntarily to the police department; [2]-Petitioner was not entitled to relief on his claim that his counsel was ineffective for failing to object to the State's DNA expert's report and testimony where petitioner failed to prove that the expert did not conduct the testing personally and therefore no confrontation or hearsay issues existed.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

July 12, 2016, Filed

State v. Lowe, 2013 Tenn. LEXIS 209 (Tenn., Feb. 25, 2013)



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The evidence was sufficient to support defendant's convictions of first-degree murder under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-13-202(a) (2010) based on aggravated child abuse under Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 39-15-401(a), -402(a)(1), where the jury could have inferred that she had a motive to kill her newborn twins to continue hiding the fact that she had become pregnant, she made preparations to hide the births, she hid evidence of the crime by cleaning the bathroom and hiding the laundry basket where one twin was found, and she knowingly treated the twins in a manner to inflict injury by placing her hand over their mouths and suffocating them; [2]-Defendant was not in custody where she accompanied the detective to the police station voluntarily, she never indicated she wanted to leave, and she was made aware of her fight to remain silent at her place of work and the police station.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Sprawling


No. W2014-02511-CCA-R9-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT JACKSON


2016 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 480



July 5, 2016, Assigned on Briefs 
July 5, 2016, Filed


NOTICE: ORDERED NOT FOR CITATION. PLEASE CONSULT THE TENNESSEE SUPREME COURT RULES.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Ordered Not for Citation November 22, 2016.
Review denied and ordered not published by State v. Sprawling, 2016 Tenn. LEXIS 847 (Tenn., Nov. 22, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 9 [*1] , Interlocutory Appeal; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Shelby County. No. 1401576. Carolyn W. Blackett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant's cooperation with the blood draw, after the officer explained to defendant that he had to give a blood sample because he had a prior DUI, did not imply actual consent and the trial court did not err in concluding that defendant's consent was not unequivocal, specific, intelligently given, and uncontaminated by duress or coercion; [2]-The fact that defendant drove a motor vehicle on the highways of Tennessee did not mean that defendant gave implied consent to the blood draw, as the privilege of driving did not alone crease consent for a forcible draw and Tenn. Code Ann. § 55-10-406 was silent as to whether a warrant was required for the mandatory blood draw.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Stripling


No. E2015-01554-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2016 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 443


April 27, 2016, Assigned on Briefs 
June 16, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 3 [*1] Appeal as of Right; Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part, Modified in Part, Reversed in Part, and Remanded. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 102315. G. Scott Green, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgments of the Criminal Court Affirmed in Part, Modified in Part, Reversed in Part, and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Tenn. Code Ann. § 40-35-121 is sufficiently precise to provide fair warning as to conduct that is covered by the statute, and it is not void for vagueness; [2]-However, § 40-35-121(b) violates substantive due process principles; [3]-Without a requirement that the offense be related to a defendant's criminal gang membership, the court fails to comprehend how § 40-35-121(b) is reasonably related to the goal of deterring criminal gang activity; [4]-The statute does not reach a substantial amount of constitutionally protected conduct, and defendant's claim that the status violated his First Amendment rights to association and expression was without merit; [5]-The evidence was sufficient to support defendant's convictions for sale and delivery of less than.5 grams of cocaine within a drug-free zone, for purposes of Tenn. Code Ann. §§ 39-17-417(a), 39-17-432(b)(1) (2010).


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part, modified in part, reversed in part, and remanded.

State v. Burton


No. E2015-00879-CCA-R3-CD


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF TENNESSEE, AT KNOXVILLE


2016 Tenn. Crim. App. LEXIS 425


March 22, 2016, Session 
June 9, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by State v. Burton, 2016 Tenn. LEXIS 755 (Tenn., Oct. 20, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Tenn. R. App. P. 3 [*1] Appeal as of Right; Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed. Appeal from the Criminal Court for Knox County. No. 103245. G. Scott Green, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Criminal Court Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The child neglect statute in Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-15-401(b) was not unconstitutionally vague because the statute was sufficiently clear to put an ordinary person of common intelligence on notice that it was a crime to knowingly fail to provide reasonable attention or supervision to a child where such an omission resulted in an adverse effect to the health and welfare of the child; [2]-The evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of aggravated child neglect under Tenn. Code Ann. § 39-15-402 as he placed the unclothed 17-month-old victim in the back of the bathtub and left the bathroom while the hot water was running; in his absence, the victim sustained second degree burns on over seven percent of his body; and he knowingly left the victim unattended under circumstances that resulted in serious bodily injury.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.
